201512	13	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Let’s ask Simon to start things off with the Desk report.	61	6
201512	14	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	61	6
201512	15	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Since the Committee met in October, expectations that liftoff will occur at this meeting have increased substantially, while the expected slope of the target rate thereafter is little changed.	61	6
201512	16	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	As liftoff expectations grew earlier in the period, broader asset prices were relatively range bound.	61	6
201512	17	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	However, late in the period, sharp commodity price declines weighed on risk sentiment.	61	6
201512	18	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	On net, domestic financial conditions tightened over the period.	61	6
201512	19	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	As shown in the top-left panel of your first exhibit, over the period the market- implied probability of liftoff at this meeting increased markedly, driven by the October FOMC statement and the better-than-expected October employment report.	61	6
201512	20	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Adjusting for year-end effects in the January federal funds futures contract, we estimate a market-implied probability of roughly 90 percent.	61	6
201512	21	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	The average probability of liftoff at this meeting, according to the Desk’s most recent dealer and buy-side surveys, is also around 90 percent.	61	6
201512	22	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	And all but one of the 51 respondents view this meeting as the most likely time of liftoff.	61	6
201512	23	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Amid the buildup in expectations regarding liftoff, there was a parallel shift up in the market-implied policy rate path, as shown in the top-right panel.	61	6
201512	24	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	The market- implied path continues to be shallow by historical standards at the initiation of tightening phases, rising by about 50 basis points per year in 2016 and 2017.	61	6
201512	25	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	According to the Desk’s surveys, the average expected pace of tightening in the first two years after liftoff, conditional on not returning to the effective lower bound, declined slightly, as shown in the middle-left panel, continuing the trend observed since we first asked about this in September 2014.	61	6
201512	26	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	On average, survey respondents now expect the target rate to increase 80 basis points in the first year after liftoff and 95 basis points in the second year.	61	6
201512	27	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Market rates over the next two years are still somewhat below the mean expectations of the target rate in the Desk’s surveys, as shown in the middle-right panel.	61	6
201512	28	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	These mean expectations are derived from survey questions eliciting probability distributions for year-end rates.	61	6
201512	29	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Importantly, the answers include assessments of the likelihood of returning to the zero bound.	61	6
201512	30	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	The dots in the panel show individual respondents’ expectations for the year-end target federal funds rate in 2016 and 2017, with the dots scaled by the proportion of respondents expecting each rate level and shaded by how likely they view a return to the effective lower bound; darker shades indicate a lower probability of returning to the effective lower bound.	61	6
201512	31	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	As you can see, the gap between market rates (the red diamonds) and the average survey expectations (the blue dashed lines) is slight for 2016 but becomes larger in 2017, and respondents that place high weight on a return to the zero lower bound have lower mean rate expectations.	61	6
201512	32	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	The medians of the survey respondents’ modal expectations regarding the federal funds rate remain slightly below the median of the SEP dots published in September.	61	6
201512	33	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Desk survey respondents generally expect a decline in the median 2017 and 2018 dots and in the median projection of the longer-run rate at this meeting.	61	6
201512	34	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	In written commentary, they highlighted persistent downward pressures on global growth and recent Federal Reserve communications on the neutral federal funds rate as underpinning these expectations.	61	6
201512	35	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Thomas will discuss the path of policy and market expectations more in his briefing.	61	6
201512	36	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Shifting to broader markets, expectations for liftoff to come at this meeting appeared to be taken largely in stride, particularly over the time period in early November during which these expectations increased to high levels.	61	6
201512	37	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	In November, domestic equity price indices and credit spreads were relatively little changed, and, as shown in the bottom-left panel, option-implied volatility across asset classes remained subdued.	61	6
201512	38	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	However, sharp declines in oil prices late in the intermeeting period appear to have had knock-on effects throughout global financial markets.	61	6
201512	39	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	These declines in oil prices are shown in the bottom-right panel.	61	6
201512	40	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Over the period, the price of front-month Brent crude dropped by about 20 percent.	61	6
201512	41	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Broader commodity prices also declined notably over the period, with the Bloomberg Industrial Metals Index falling by roughly 10 percent.	61	6
201512	42	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	While contacts largely attribute the decline in oil prices to persistent oversupply—especially following the most recent OPEC meeting—broad-based weakness in commodity prices likely in part reflects ongoing concerns about global growth.	61	6
201512	43	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	The commodity price declines had adverse effects on high-yield corporate credit markets, as reflected in the widening in high-yield spreads shown in the top-left panel of your next exhibit.	61	6
201512	44	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	The widening was most pronounced in energy credits (the dark blue line), with spreads, on average, up 200 basis points over the period.	61	6
201512	45	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	However, there was also a more broad-based selloff, with high-yield spreads ex energy widening by 80 basis points.	61	6
201512	46	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	As part of this, US high-yield mutual funds and ETFs saw outflows of $4.5 billion for the week ending December 9, up from an average outflow of about $1 billion over the prior month.	61	6
201512	47	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	And as was widely publicized last week, one open-ended high-yield mutual fund that had invested in lower-quality corporate bonds gated investors amid persistent redemption requests.	61	6
201512	48	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Commodity price declines also continued to serve as a headwind to inflation compensation and emerging market asset prices.	61	6
201512	49	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Five-year and five-year, five-year- forward inflation compensation was little changed on net and remains well below historical averages and the Federal Reserve’s inflation objective, as shown in the top- right panel.	61	6
201512	50	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Meanwhile, the JP Morgan Emerging Market Currency Index declined by 3 percent, and the MSCI Emerging Market Equity Index fell by over 10 percent.	61	6
201512	51	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	The onshore and offshore renminbi depreciated against the US dollar, as shown in the middle-left panel, taking the renminbi to levels weaker against the dollar than those seen following the devaluation in August.	61	6
201512	52	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Further, the basis between the onshore and offshore renminbi widened in recent weeks, as shown in grey in this panel, likely reflecting a reduced desire by Chinese officials to intervene in the wake of the announcement of the renminbi’s inclusion in the SDR basket and ahead of FOMC liftoff.	61	6
201512	53	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	China’s leadership repeatedly stressed the strength of the renminbi on a trade- weighted basis, and many expect that in the future they will measure the renminbi against a basket of currencies rather than considering only the U.S dollar.	61	6
201512	54	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	More broadly, while dollar strength was most pronounced against commodity- linked currencies, the dollar appreciated modestly against the currencies of all major US trading partners over the period, as shown in the dark blue lines in the middle- right panel.	61	6
201512	55	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	The Bloomberg Dollar Spot Index increased by about 1 percent, pushing year-to-date gains to nearly 8 percent.	61	6
201512	56	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	The ongoing theme of monetary policy divergence, particularly between the Federal Reserve and other major central banks, such as the ECB, continued to serve as a tailwind to US dollar strength.	61	6
201512	57	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	While on net the euro-to-dollar exchange rate was little changed on the period, the euro did touch its weakest level against the dollar since March, as expectations of Fed and ECB policy diverged starkly.	61	6
201512	58	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	This divergence can be seen in the spread between US and German two-year nominal yields, shown in the bottom-left panel, which reached year-to-date highs just ahead of the December ECB meeting.	61	6
201512	59	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	At that meeting, the ECB announced an array of additional easing measures, including a 10 basis point cut to its deposit facility rate to negative 30 basis points, an extension of its asset purchases by at least six months, and an expansion of its public- sector purchase program to include reinvestments and local and regional bonds.	61	6
201512	60	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Nevertheless, market expectations for the extent of ECB easing had become quite lofty ahead of the meeting, and the announcement led to an abrupt tightening of euro- area financial conditions, including a sharp increase in euro-area sovereign yields.	61	6
201512	61	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Interestingly, a substantial portion of the rise in these yields passed through into Treasury yields, particularly at the long end of the curve, as shown in the bottom-right panel.	61	6
201512	62	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	This highlights, as did the taper tantrum, the correlation in global term premiums and financial conditions more broadly.	61	6
201512	63	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	As I noted earlier, the move to an almost fully priced-in increase for the federal funds target range appeared to be taken largely in stride during November, but this occurred with no reevaluation of the path of policy.	61	6
201512	64	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	As is clear from both the taper tantrum and the recent experience of the ECB, markets can be very sensitive to changes in policy or communications—at times, it appears, for no good reason.	61	6
201512	65	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Thus, there is still likely event risk surrounding the announcement of the Committee’s decision tomorrow, particularly given the turbulence in markets in the past few days, although the major surprise to markets would be no change in the target range.	61	6
201512	66	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	I’ll begin on exhibit 3 and provide a review of money markets, market functioning, and Desk operations.	61	6
201512	67	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	Over the intermeeting period, the staff continued testing the Federal Reserve’s policy normalization tools, with the overnight RRP operations continuing to provide a soft floor under short-term interest rates, including around month-ends.	61	6
201512	68	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the top-left panel, outside month-end, the effective federal funds rate printed between 12 and 14 basis points.	61	6
201512	69	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	Treasury bill and repo rates fluctuated more notably amid the shifts in bill supply following the suspension of the debt ceiling.	61	6
201512	70	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the top-right panel, overnight RRP take-up averaged $105 billion over the period, increasing on month-ends.	61	6
201512	71	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	And as shown in grey, Federal Reserve reverse repurchases with foreign official institutions, otherwise known as the foreign RP pool, hit record levels of over $200 billion early in the period.	61	6
201512	72	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	Usage of both operations continued to be sensitive to the level of market rates.	61	6
201512	73	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	As you can see, usage declined later in the period, reflecting the impact of higher Treasury bill rates.	61	6
201512	74	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	Over the intermeeting period, the Desk announced plans to offer a total of $300 billion in three term RRP operations crossing year-end.	61	6
201512	75	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	We will provide an update on the intended plans for these operations at the end of the FOMC meeting tomorrow, as the details will depend upon the Committee’s policy decision.	61	6
201512	76	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	As Simon noted, this intermeeting period saw a significant increase in the likelihood market participants place on liftoff occurring at this meeting.	61	6
201512	77	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	The middle- left panel shows expectations for the levels of three overnight interest rates following liftoff, as implied by financial market contracts and the Desk’s surveys.	61	6
201512	78	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	We calculated the market-implied post-liftoff levels of the effective federal funds rate and GCF repo rate using futures contracts adjusted for expected year-end movements, assuming that the median probability assigned to December liftoff from the Desk’s surveys of 90 percent is currently priced in.	61	6
201512	79	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	In addition to the point estimates represented by the blue dots, we calculated a range for implied post-liftoff levels based on different assumptions about the perceived probability of liftoff, shown in the light blue shaded area.	61	6
201512	80	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	As you can see, the market- and survey-based measures for the effective federal funds, GCF, and triparty repo rates suggest that these overnight rates are expected to shift up by around 20 basis points from their current levels, to within the target range of 25 to 50 basis points that market participants expect to prevail after liftoff.	61	6
201512	81	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	These rates are also expected to retain their current configuration, with the effective federal funds rate below the interdealer GCF repo rate and slightly above the triparty repo rate.	61	6
201512	82	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	However, it appears that the pass-through of the increase in the target range to market rates is expected to be slightly less than one for one, in part due to expectations that the ON RRP offering rate following liftoff will increase by only 20 basis points relative to an increase of 25 basis points in the target range.	61	6
201512	83	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	As I noted, when calculating the overnight rates implied by futures contracts, we assumed that year-end conditions would be similar to what we have seen during the past few quarter-ends.	61	6
201512	84	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	While market participants expect some volatility in money markets related to year-end, we have no reason to expect that conditions will be materially worse than in recent year-end periods.	61	6
201512	85	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the middle-right panel, respondents to the Desk’s surveys continue to broadly expect ample capacity, or headroom, in overnight RRP operations following liftoff, either through an elevated or suspended aggregate cap.	61	6
201512	86	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	This is reflected in the white boxes, shown in the panel, which are calculated based on expectations for the difference between overnight RRP capacity and demand.	61	6
201512	87	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	The expectation of ample capacity has likely contributed to confidence in the Federal Reserve’s ability to control short-term interest rates following liftoff and around the year-end.	61	6
201512	88	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	While we don’t have reason to expect major dislocations associated with liftoff around year-end, I’d like to highlight some developments across markets that contacts have noted as potentially pointing to important structural changes in financial intermediation.	61	6
201512	89	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	Recall that at prior meetings, we have updated the Committee on the widening in spreads within the Treasury repo market.	61	6
201512	90	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	This has resulted from dealers with large, stable repo funding bases requiring increased compensation to intermediate between money funds in the triparty repo market and the smaller, less creditworthy dealers that seek to borrow in the interdealer, or GCF, market.	61	6
201512	91	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the bottom-left panel, the spread between the volume-weighted average rates in the interdealer segment and the broader triparty market has widened.	61	6
201512	92	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	This spread, which averaged only a couple of basis points during 2013, has widened to over 10 basis points and has spiked as much as 30 basis points on quarter-ends.	61	6
201512	93	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	The widening in this spread has had a direct impact on the cost of intermediation in the Treasury repo market.	61	6
201512	94	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	It has also been noted as having more indirect impacts in other markets.	61	6
201512	95	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	As illustrated in the bottom-right panel, the US interest rate swap spread—the difference between the LIBOR-based swap rate and corresponding Treasury yield, shown for the five-year tenor in the dark blue line—has narrowed over recent months and is now negative at maturities of five years and beyond.	61	6
201512	96	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	In theory, swap rates should be higher than Treasury yields of equivalent maturity because they reference three-month LIBOR, which has credit risk.	61	6
201512	97	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	The moves in swap spreads have been associated with developments that suggest they may be temporary.	61	6
201512	98	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	For example, the narrowing coincided with increased foreign-reserve manager sales of US Treasury securities—sales that should put upward pressure on Treasury yields—and elevated realized and expected corporate bond issuance, which should put downward pressure on swap rates.	61	6
201512	99	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	An additional factor cited that may suggest a more persistent shift in these spreads, however, has been an increase in the cost of financing Treasury securities, something that is necessary for speculative arbitrage that would serve to restore a positive swap spread.	61	6
201512	100	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	The increase in financing costs is reflected in the recent inversion in the spread between the three-month LIBOR rate and the equivalent-maturity Treasury GC repo rate, also shown in the bottom-right panel.	61	6
201512	101	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	This inversion has been driven primarily by the increase in the term GC repo rate, consistent with the rise in the repo market spreads I noted a moment ago in panel 17.	61	6
201512	102	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	In the most recent Desk surveys, respondents were asked to rate the importance of various factors in explaining the recent narrowing in swap spreads.	61	6
201512	103	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	As summarized in the top-left panel of your fourth exhibit, respondents assigned the highest rating to “increased balance sheet cost for cash products,” with 42 of 50 respondents assigning their highest rating to this factor.	61	6
201512	104	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	Some pricing anomalies have also emerged in foreign exchange swap basis spreads.	61	6
201512	105	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	Over recent months, we have seen the spreads across a number of currencies widen, as shown in the top-right panel, suggesting a higher cost of borrowing dollars offshore after hedging the corresponding foreign exchange risk.	61	6
201512	106	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	The widening does not seem to reflect current funding stress in offshore funding markets, and has instead been attributed to increased demand for US dollars via the FX swap market as a byproduct of monetary policy divergence, as well as increased demand for dollar funding over year-end.	61	6
201512	107	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	This widening would normally be arbitraged away by banks that would lend at a high premium via the FX swap market.	61	6
201512	108	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	However, contacts have suggested that the elevated cost of expanding their balance sheets to do so has deterred banks from engaging in this activity, particularly ahead of year-end.	61	6
201512	109	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	To summarize, the market dynamics I described in Treasury repo and interest rate and FX swaps appear to be, at least in part, a byproduct of the increased costs financial institutions face when expanding their balance sheets to intermediate certain market activity.	61	6
201512	110	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	The resulting shifts in market rates and spreads could have implications for the monetary policy transmission process.	61	6
201512	111	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	The next few panels focus on reinvestments.	61	6
201512	112	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	As the perceived likelihood of liftoff occurring at this meeting has risen, market participants have also been focused on other parts of the normalization process, including the reinvestments of principal payments on Treasury securities and agency MBS.	61	6
201512	113	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the middle-left panel, the median respondent to the Desk’s surveys now expects the FOMC will cease some or all reinvestments of Treasury securities and agency MBS approximately 12 months following liftoff, roughly 3 months later than was expected in October and 6 months later than was expected one year ago.	61	6
201512	114	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	In explaining the changes to their expectations, respondents focused on recent FOMC communications on conditions surrounding the end of reinvestment policy specifically and the gradual path of normalization more generally.	61	6
201512	115	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the middle-right panel, conditional on reinvestments being phased out over time, the median respondent expects this to occur over a one-year period following a change in the reinvestment policy, suggesting that a full cessation of reinvestments would not be expected to occur until roughly two years following liftoff.	61	6
201512	116	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	Lastly, I should note that in light of the large volume of Treasury maturities scheduled in early 2016, the Desk has fielded an increasing number of inquiries on the mechanics of the Treasury reinvestment policy.	61	6
201512	117	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	As we discussed in June, and as reflected in the June minutes, the Desk will continue to roll over maturing Treasury securities at auction.	61	6
201512	118	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	As summarized in the bottom-left panel, this is accomplished by placing bids for the SOMA at Treasury auctions equal in par amount to the value of holdings maturing on the issue date of the securities being auctioned.	61	6
201512	119	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	The bids are allocated proportionally across those securities being auctioned based on the announced offering amounts.	61	6
201512	120	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	SOMA holdings are currently limited to 70 percent of the total outstanding amount of any one Treasury security.	61	6
201512	121	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	The Desk observes this when rolling over maturing securities.	61	6
201512	122	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	In order to provide additional clarity on this question to the public in advance of upcoming maturing of Treasury securities, the Desk plans to publish FAQs to the public website shortly after this meeting that will outline the details of the Treasury securities reinvestment policy.	61	6
201512	123	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	We have copies of these FAQs if you would like to review them.	61	6
201512	124	2015-12-16	meeting	LOGAN	Before I turn the briefing back over to Simon for updates on some longer-term issues, we’ll be happy to take questions.	61	6

201512	155	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Seeing none, Simon, why don’t you proceed.	62	6
201512	156	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	I thought it would be useful to update the Committee on several other issues.	61	6
201512	157	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	As noted in the revised notification for the year-end term RRP operations, the September 30 two-day term RRP operation was not authorized under the March term RRP testing resolution, as the resolution had only authorized conducting term RRP operations through September 29.	61	6
201512	158	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	There are multiple layers of review for open market operations that all missed this issue, and it was discovered only in the review process for the December term operations.	61	6
201512	159	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	We are continuing to assess what adjustments to the control environment could be effective in preventing this type of occurrence in the future and how we can better routinize the detection process, particularly prior to the ratification of open market operations at FOMC meetings.	61	6
201512	160	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	The public announcement of the September 30 term RRP operation did cite the testing resolution, and in the 2015 annual report on domestic operations we will note the deviation.	61	6
201512	161	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	The revised data collection for FR 2420 has been proceeding smoothly.	61	6
201512	162	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	As can be seen in the first panel of exhibit 5, the volumes collected for the federal funds market have increased, and the staff is confident that the data we are receiving is of sufficient quality to execute on the plan to change the underlying data source for the publication of the effective federal funds rate to the FR 2420.	61	6
201512	163	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	The switchover is planned to occur at the start of March, and at that time we would also adjust the calculation method to the volume-weighted median from the volume-weighted mean.	61	6
201512	164	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	In addition, we are now collecting a very large volume of Eurodollar transactions and plan to also start publishing the overnight bank funding rate, or OBFR.	61	6
201512	165	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	The top-right panel shows a comparison of the effective federal funds rate and OBFR from the revised data collection, with those rates calculated using the brokered data.	61	6
201512	166	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	These differences are small.	61	6
201512	167	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	The Desk plans to announce the switchover date on January 6, following the release of the minutes of this meeting.	61	6
201512	168	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	As outlined in the middle-left panel, this public announcement would also include details about efforts to increase transparency and about policies intended to align the production of the EFFR and OBFR with international standards for financial benchmarks, as described in a memo sent to the Committee last week.	61	6
201512	169	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	An additional advantage of the FR 2420 data over the data we receive from the brokers is that we can publish more details about the unsecured overnight market.	61	6
201512	170	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	The memo outlines the summary statistics we would include with the daily publication of the EFFR and OBFR.	61	6
201512	171	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	The staff is considering whether additional data should be released with a lag, and we would welcome your feedback on this and other details of the plan.	61	6
201512	172	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Since 2014, we have been able to analyze secured money markets using daily transaction data from the triparty repo market, as noted in the middle-right panel.	61	6
201512	173	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	The Desk has found this very useful in its analysis of the overnight and term RRP operations as well as in its overall market monitoring efforts.	61	6
201512	174	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	In 2014, the Federal Reserve convened the Alternative Reference Rates Committee, or ARRC, a group of major US dollar swap dealers tasked with identifying robust alternative reference rates.	61	6
201512	175	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Staff members working to support the ARRC, under Governor Powell’s leadership, have been assessing whether there might be a role for the official sector to produce an alternative reference rate based on overnight secured transactions, particularly given that the Desk already produces one such rate internally.	61	6
201512	176	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	The staff is currently investigating the possibility of the Federal Reserve Bank of New York publicly producing such a rate with the support of the Office of Financial Research.	61	6
201512	177	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	At the June meeting, the staff updated the Committee regarding a review of the Federal Reserve’s counterparty framework.	61	6
201512	178	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	At that time, we noted that the current framework is serving the Committee well while highlighting potential improvements in the administration of the counterparties.	61	6
201512	179	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	For the primary dealers, we are also investigating the appropriate financial condition criteria, following the discussion at the June meeting.	61	6
201512	180	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Our assessment has also been informed by the Treasury Operations Counterparty program and the Mortgage Operations Counterparty program, or MOC.	61	6
201512	181	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Details on operational results from the MOC are contained in the bottom panel.	61	6
201512	182	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	In these programs, the Desk conducted outright transactions with smaller broker-dealers.	61	6
201512	183	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Our evaluation is that the very small operational benefits associated with transacting with smaller broker-dealers are greatly outweighed by the costs associated with managing such relationships.	61	6
201512	184	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Thus, we are unlikely to recommend that dealers with less than $50 million in capital—the maximum capital of MOC participants—be eligible to be a primary dealer.	61	6
201512	185	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	The staff will continue to study potential adjustments to the counterparty frameworks in the context of a more sophisticated counterparty risk management approach that relies less on capital.	61	6
201512	186	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Once we have this framework in place, we will present draft revised administrative policies to the Committee for feedback.	61	6
201512	187	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Recall that in the discussion of the modernization of the Domestic Authorization last January, I suggested simplifying the description of eligible counterparties.	61	6
201512	188	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	The Committee decided it preferred to wait for some of the results of the counterparty review before considering this change.	61	6
201512	189	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Unless the Committee has strong views in favor of making this change in January, I would recommend waiting for the revised counterparty administrative policies before addressing this issue again.	61	6
201512	190	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	The staff have also been working on modernizing the documents related to foreign operations.	61	6
201512	191	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	This work has uncovered a number of legacy issues related to earlier periods of active foreign operations.	61	6
201512	192	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Further, the structure of the documents is not symmetric with the domestic side, and we see value in moving to a structure in which the Committee more explicitly directs the current and potential future operations of the Desk.	61	6
201512	193	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	The form of this direction may be influenced in part by the results of a project evaluating the current foreign-reserves management framework.	61	6
201512	194	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	This framework has been strained by the negative rates in the euro area, as can be seen in the top-left panel of your final exhibit.	61	6
201512	195	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	We project overall income on the euro portfolio to turn negative next year under our current investment approach.	61	6
201512	196	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	We hope to be ready to present recommendations to the Committee at the March meeting, although there is a significant risk that it could take longer.	61	6
201512	197	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Consequently, we recommend deferring any changes in the documents controlling foreign operations until the foreign reserves management review is complete.	61	6
201512	198	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Finally, the Desk, working closely with Board staff members, has been developing a formal structure for assessing the full range of operations that are readily available for implementation, as well as the lead time required to implement new or dormant operations under appropriate risk controls.	61	6
201512	199	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	As shown in the top-right panel, the structure starts by cataloguing all existing and potential operations and facilities and assigning each to one of five readiness categories.	61	6
201512	200	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	This structure allows us to comprehensively assess the readiness of operations and employ clear standards for testing, training, and technological development.	61	6
201512	201	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	It is important to emphasize that it is appropriate for the vast majority of operations and facilities in the extended and significant development categories to remain there.	61	6
201512	202	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	As an example of an active use of this framework, consider the recent test of accepting yen for dollars that completed a series of small value tests of our ability to receive foreign currency from central banks in the active standing swap network.	61	6
201512	203	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	The completion of these tests moved this operation to “in production standby” from “rapid deployment.”	61	6
201512	204	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Such live operational tests are important to validate that an operation remains in standby mode.	61	6
201512	205	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	This is why we ran a repo test this intermeeting period as well.	61	6
201512	206	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Such testing does identify issues that require attention to maintain the standby status.	61	6
201512	207	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	For example, the recent TDF test exposed a small glitch in how funds are matured from TDF accounts due to software changes.	61	6
201512	208	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	The testing allowed San Francisco and Board staff members to fix the glitch prior to liftoff.	61	6
201512	209	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Another advantage of such testing is that when problems occur, we can test backup capacity.	61	6
201512	210	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	This happened last week in the live testing of the overnight RRP, when a switch to a new version of FedTrade produced erroneous settlement instructions for some counterparties, requiring a manual contingency to be deployed.	61	6
201512	211	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	As we build out the operational readiness structure, it is likely we will present to the Committee a small value testing plan for the year rather than notifications for each individual test.	61	6
201512	212	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	To conclude, the staff have conducted extensive tests of the tools that the Committee might want to deploy during the early stages of normalization and are confident in their operational integrity.	61	6
201512	213	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	If the Committee decides to raise the target range tomorrow, then starting on Thursday, we will begin our daily operational call at 9:00 am to allow for more discussion and analysis among the staff and move the morning financial market update call to 9:30 am  Committee participants and their staff are welcome to join these calls.	61	6
201512	214	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	Thank you Madam Chair.	61	6
201512	215	2015-12-16	meeting	POTTER	That completes our prepared remarks.	61	6

201512	229	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	11	1

201512	231	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	The top panels of your first exhibit review labor market conditions, which have continued to improve in recent months.	11	1
201512	232	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	As indicated in the inset box in panel 1, total nonfarm payroll employment rose 210,000 in November, following a robust increase of 300,000 in October.	11	1
201512	233	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	As shown by the black line, over the past three months, payrolls have increased at an average monthly pace of 220,000, similar to the pace of recent years.	11	1
201512	234	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	The unemployment rate, shown in Panel 2, was 5 percent in both October and November, slightly lower than in the third quarter.	11	1
201512	235	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Over the past 12 months, the unemployment rate has fallen ¾ percentage point.	11	1
201512	236	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	The labor force participation rate, shown in the middle-left panel, ticked up to 62.5 percent in November.	11	1
201512	237	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Over the past 12 months, the participation rate has moved down 0.4 percentage point, the same pace of decline as for the trend (the blue line).	11	1
201512	238	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	As shown in the middle-right panel, manufacturing output edged up only slightly in the first half of the year.	11	1
201512	239	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	We currently estimate that manufacturing IP rose 3½ percent at an annual rate in the third quarter, and we anticipate a small increase in the current quarter.	11	1
201512	240	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	November data will be released tomorrow morning.	11	1
201512	241	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Panel 5 presents the staff outlook for consumer spending.	11	1
201512	242	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	We currently estimate that real PCE increased at a 2½ percent annual rate in the current quarter, a bit less than in the third quarter.	11	1
201512	243	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Some of that downtick reflects the effects of unseasonably warm weather, which held down use of energy-related utility services.	11	1
201512	244	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Averaging across this quarter and next, we expect real PCE to rise about 3 percent at an annual rate.	11	1
201512	245	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	After the Tealbook closed, we received the November retail sales report.	11	1
201512	246	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	The latest readings, summarized in the inset box, are consistent with the Tealbook outlook.	11	1
201512	247	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	As shown in the bottom-right panel, we continue to expect real GDP to increase at about a 2 percent annual rate over the second half of this year and in the first quarter of next year.	11	1
201512	248	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	That pace is a bit faster than our estimate of potential GDP growth.	11	1
201512	249	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Our medium-term outlook for real GDP is shown in panel 1 of your next exhibit.	11	1
201512	250	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Over the medium term, we expect real GDP to increase about in line with the pace of recent years.	11	1
201512	251	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	In particular, we’re forecasting real GDP to rise 2½ percent next year and about 2 percent in each of 2017 and 2018.	11	1
201512	252	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	The top-right panel discusses some of the key factors shaping our outlook.	11	1
201512	253	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	As noted in the first bullet and shown in panel 3, net exports are expected to be a substantial drag on GDP growth in 2016 and 2017, reflecting the ongoing effects of the appreciation of the dollar since the middle of last year.	11	1
201512	254	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Joe Gruber will discuss the net export outlook in more detail in his presentation.	11	1
201512	255	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	We think a number of other factors will support GDP growth over the medium term.	11	1
201512	256	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	As shown in panel 4, after several years when fiscal policy was a substantial drag on real activity, it more recently has provided a modest degree of stimulus.	11	1
201512	257	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	We expect that to continue next year as spending authorized by the bipartisan budget agreement ramps up.	11	1
201512	258	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	In addition, we anticipate that consumer spending will continue to be supported by the high level of household wealth, shown in panel 5.	11	1
201512	259	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Panel 6 shows the staff outlook for the unemployment rate.	11	1
201512	260	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	With output gains forecast to exceed the staff’s estimate of potential growth, the unemployment rate continues to fall and reaches 4½ percent by the end of 2018.	11	1
201512	261	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	The pace of improvement is somewhat less than in recent years despite a similar rate of increase in real GDP.	11	1
201512	262	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	As you can see in panel 1, we anticipate that potential output will rise somewhat more rapidly in the medium term than has been the case in the recent past.	11	1
201512	263	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Thus, the same increase in real GDP leads to a smaller change in resource utilization and, as a consequence, a smaller reduction in the unemployment rate.	11	1
201512	264	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	The dashed red line shows the outlook for the unemployment rate as of the June Tealbook.	11	1
201512	265	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Our near- term outlook for the unemployment rate is about ¼ percentage point lower than in June.	11	1
201512	266	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	By 2018, the downward revision is a bit more than ½ percentage point.	11	1
201512	267	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Your third exhibit presents our outlook for inflation, starting with the near term in the top-left panel.	11	1
201512	268	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	As of the December Tealbook, we expected headline PCE inflation would be around zero in the current quarter as well as in the first quarter of next year, held down by falling energy prices.	11	1
201512	269	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	We anticipated that core PCE prices would rise at an annual rate of 1¼ percent in the current quarter and a bit more in the first quarter.	11	1
201512	270	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Since the Tealbook closed, we’ve received PPI data and, this morning, the November CPI.	11	1
201512	271	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Taking these data into account, we now expect near-term inflation to be slightly lower than at the time of the Tealbook.	11	1
201512	272	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Notably, current-quarter core PCE inflation would be 1 percent rather than 1¼ percent.	11	1
201512	273	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	The top-right panel shows 12-month changes in total and core PCE prices.	11	1
201512	274	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	The plotted series end with the staff’s estimate for November as of the Tealbook.	11	1
201512	275	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	With the latest data in hand, we now estimate that overall PCE prices (the dashed red line) rose only ¼ percent over the 12 months ended in November, just a touch lower than the Tealbook figure that is plotted.	11	1
201512	276	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	The solid black line shows the 12-month change in core PCE prices.	11	1
201512	277	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Taking into account the CPI and PPI data, we now estimate the 12-month change through November to be 1.3 percent—again, just a touch lower than the figure that’s plotted.	11	1
201512	278	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Panel 3 shows the staff’s outlook for core PCE inflation over the medium term, along with a decomposition of the key factors driving the forecast.	11	1
201512	279	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Overall, we see core inflation rising from 1.3 percent this year to 1.9 percent by 2018.	11	1
201512	280	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	As can be seen in line 2, in the staff’s view, the recent declines in energy and import prices have held down core inflation by about ½ percentage point this year and will have a similar effect next year.	11	1
201512	281	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	By 2018, however, energy and import prices are a neutral influence.	11	1
201512	282	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	As shown in line 3, we also anticipate that rising resource utilization will boost inflation over the next several years.	11	1
201512	283	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	The effect is expected to be slight, however, reflecting the staff’s view that the economy’s implicit “Phillips curve” is very flat.	11	1
201512	284	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Line 4 presents the effects of other factors.	11	1
201512	285	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Among other things, we anticipate that unusually low medical price increases will restrain inflation for the next year or so but will be essentially neutral by 2018.	11	1
201512	286	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Finally, the staff estimates that underlying inflation is currently 1.8 percent and will remain at that level for the next several years.	11	1
201512	287	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	We expect underlying inflation eventually to move up to the Committee’s long-run objective.	11	1
201512	288	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	As can be seen in the middle-right panel, our forecast for core PCE inflation (the black line) is a bit lower than we wrote down in June (the dashed red line), especially next year.	11	1
201512	289	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	The near-term downward revision mostly reflects lower energy and import prices than in June; the projection for 2018 is about unchanged.	11	1
201512	290	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Panel 5 shows the outlook for overall PCE inflation.	11	1
201512	291	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Energy is once again the culprit for the near-term downward revision since June.	11	1
201512	292	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Once the drag due to the behavior of oil prices fades, we continue to expect overall PCE inflation to move in line with core inflation.	11	1
201512	293	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Panel 6 shows recent data on hourly compensation.	11	1
201512	294	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Over the 12 months ended in September, hourly compensation as measured by the ECI (the dot-dash black line) rose about 2 percent, a bit less than over the preceding 12-month period.	11	1
201512	295	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Hourly compensation from the productivity and costs program posted large gains in the second and third quarters and, as can be seen in the solid blue line, was up 3½ percent over the most recent four quarters.	11	1
201512	296	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	While that is a step-up from the sluggish pace of recent years, this is a volatile series and, for now, we are not taking too much signal from its recent acceleration.	11	1
201512	297	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Your final exhibit highlights two of the alternative scenarios that were presented in the Tealbook, in which we consider the consequences of a recession when the economy is still near the zero lower bound on nominal interest rates.	11	1
201512	298	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	As noted in panel 1, the bulk of the statistical evidence suggests that recessions do not die of old age (that is, the chance of a recession does not increase as time passes).	11	1
201512	299	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Nonetheless, based on the average occurrence of recessions since 1960, there is about a 15 to 20 percent chance of a recession occurring in any given year—and thus close to a 50 percent chance over the next three years.	11	1
201512	300	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	In the Tealbook scenarios, we considered the implications of a recession that starts in 2016:Q2, when the federal funds rate is forecast to still be close to zero.	11	1
201512	301	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	We carried out the simulations using the staff’s EDO model, which is a DSGE model of the US domestic economy.	11	1
201512	302	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	As discussed in panel 2, our recession scenario reflects shocks to the model that have been chosen to replicate the average behavior of real GDP and the federal funds rate in the five more moderate recessions since 1960.	11	1
201512	303	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Over those recessions, real GDP fell an average of ¾ percent from peak to trough, and the federal funds rate fell 275 basis points.	11	1
201512	304	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	This decline in the federal funds rate is much larger and more rapid than would be implied by the inertial version of the Taylor rule that we typically use in our Tealbook scenarios.	11	1
201512	305	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	As is our usual practice, we assume no additional unconventional policy response.	11	1
201512	306	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	The middle row shows the implications of these shocks under two assumptions about monetary policy—with and without the zero lower bound imposed.	11	1
201512	307	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Without the lower bound on nominal interest rates, as can be seen in the blue dot-dash line in panel 3, the unemployment rate peaks in the middle of 2017 at just over 6 percent.	11	1
201512	308	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Inflation—in the middle panel—stays at 1¼ percent next year rather than rising as in the baseline.	11	1
201512	309	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	With the federal funds rate at around 50 basis points before the recession starts, it falls just below minus 2 percent by the end of next year.	11	1
201512	310	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	When we assume, plausibly, that the federal funds rate can’t fall below zero, the outcomes for the economy are worse.	11	1
201512	311	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	As shown in the red dashed line in panel 3, in this case, the unemployment rate reaches nearly 7 percent.	11	1
201512	312	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	The federal funds rate—in the panel at the far right—returns to its effective lower bound in the second quarter of next year and remains at that level through 2017.	11	1
201512	313	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	As I just noted, the scenario includes the assumption that the Committee does not make use of any of its unconventional tools.	11	1
201512	314	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	If the Committee does use unconventional policy, outcomes would likely be better than those represented by the red dashed lines.	11	1
201512	315	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	The bottom panel raises some additional considerations.	11	1
201512	316	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	As noted in the first bullet, over the course of the medium term, the funds rate rises in the baseline projection.	11	1
201512	317	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Thus, starting in 2018, there would be room, under the baseline, to accommodate a 275 basis point cut in the federal funds rate.	11	1
201512	318	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	It is worth noting, however, that here we have assumed a moderate recession.	11	1
201512	319	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	If we take into account the severe recessions as well, the average drop in the federal funds rate would have been 400 basis points.	11	1
201512	320	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Indeed, even in a moderate recession, a funds rate cut of 275 basis points may be smaller than desirable.	11	1
201512	321	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	For example, in these scenarios, the EDO model’s estimate of the equilibrium federal funds rate drops by 650 basis points.	11	1
201512	322	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Joe Gruber will continue our presentation.	11	1
201512	323	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	Thank you.	11	1
201512	324	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	Compared with the turbulence in international financial markets that preceded your meeting in September, international conditions now appear considerably more stable.	11	1
201512	325	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	Foreign GDP growth is strengthening and financial markets remained relatively calm over much of the intermeeting period even as the probability of liftoff approached certainty.	11	1
201512	326	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	Over the past week, markets have become a bit more jittery, with emerging market currencies depreciating and spreads widening, though for reasons we generally do not pin on liftoff.	11	1
201512	327	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	In this context, our baseline forecast does not suggest adverse consequences arising from liftoff for either the foreign economies or the US external sector, but risks remain that bear continued close monitoring.	11	1
201512	328	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	As shown in the top table of exhibit 5, after a very weak second quarter, our projection of a pickup in foreign GDP growth in the third quarter (line 1) appears to have materialized.	11	1
201512	329	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	In the emerging market economies (EMEs), emerging Asia excluding China (line 3) enjoyed an especially strong step-up, supported by a stabilization of exports, as can be seen in panel 2, following substantial swings over the preceding half year.	11	1
201512	330	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	Chinese growth remained brisk (line 4), bolstered by retail sales (the red line in panel 3) and notwithstanding a dip in industrial production (the black line) that has already begun to fade.	11	1
201512	331	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	The pace of activity also stepped up in the advanced foreign economies (AFEs) (line 6), with bouncebacks in Canada (line 7), after declining oil investment pushed down GDP in the first half, and Japan (line 8).	11	1
201512	332	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	Growth in the euro area (line 9) and the United Kingdom (line 10) disappointed slightly, but the indicators for the fourth quarter, including composite PMIs (shown in panel 4), support our outlook for strengthening European growth.	11	1
201512	333	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	One particularly dark spot has been Brazil, whose GDP (line 5 in the table) continued to plummet in the third quarter as political turmoil weighed on confidence and investment, driving down industrial production (the red line in panel 5) and pushing up unemployment (the black line).	11	1
201512	334	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	We do not expect Brazilian GDP to bottom out until the middle of next year, and we have downgraded our outlook yet again as stubbornly high inflation constrains monetary policy and political problems block implementation of needed fiscal and structural policies.	11	1
201512	335	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	Returning to line 1 in the table, the overall foreign outlook is basically unchanged from the October Tealbook.	11	1
201512	336	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	Activity is expected to accelerate a bit next year, supported by accommodative monetary policy and easing credit conditions in the AFEs.	11	1
201512	337	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	In contrast to most economies we forecast, growth in China is expected to edge down gradually over the projection period, as the economy continues to rebalance away from investment and potential growth moderates.	11	1
201512	338	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	For many, but not all, economies, low oil prices are expected to boost growth, a positive impetus that has only gotten larger in light of the recent price declines.	11	1
201512	339	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	The price of Brent crude oil, the black line in panel 6, fell to just below $38 per barrel yesterday, only slightly above its trough during the global financial crisis, as global oil production remains strong and inventories accumulate.	11	1
201512	340	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	Prices came under further pressure after the recent OPEC meeting provided little indication that the cartel would take any action to reign in supply for the foreseeable future.	11	1
201512	341	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	We expect oil prices to edge up gradually during the forecast period, in part supported by declines in US production.	11	1
201512	342	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	Prices for industrial metals (the red line in panel 6) have also continued their steep decline.	11	1
201512	343	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	The higher dollar and resilient supply have played an important role in pushing down prices, as have market concerns over the strength of demand, particularly from China, for metals.	11	1
201512	344	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	Declining energy prices have been a major contributor to low inflation globally, supporting continued accommodative monetary policy by the major foreign central banks, as discussed in your next exhibit.	11	1
201512	345	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	As shown across the top three panels, headline inflation in the third quarter was near zero in the euro area, Japan, and the United Kingdom.	11	1
201512	346	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	Core inflation, though higher, is also quite subdued.	11	1
201512	347	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	Diminishing slack is expected to push up core inflation, with even steeper increases in headline inflation as oil prices flatten out.	11	1
201512	348	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	That said, inflation is expected to remain below target in both the euro area and Japan through the end of 2018.	11	1
201512	349	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	Referencing subdued inflation, the ECB announced a number of policy measures on December 3, as discussed earlier by Simon and outlined in panel 4, including an extension of its quantitative easing program and a 10 basis point cut in its deposit rate to minus 0.3 percent.	11	1
201512	350	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	As shown in panel 5, the ECB’s deposit rate (the green line) has been negative since mid-2014, pulling other short-term lending rates into negative territory as well without any noticeable disruption to European money markets.	11	1
201512	351	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	We expect the ECB to leave its policy rate (the green line in panel 6) at its current level until the end of 2018.	11	1
201512	352	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	The Bank of Japan did not announce any new measures at its October and November meetings, despite revising down its inflation outlook, but it continues to purchase assets at a rapid pace.	11	1
201512	353	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	In the United Kingdom, markets were struck by the dovish tone of the Bank of England’s November Inflation Report, including the announcement that it would not consider reducing its asset holdings until the policy rate normalized to about 2 percent, a higher threshold than many had previously expected.	11	1
201512	354	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	We expect the BOE to begin hiking its policy rate (the blue line in panel 6) in the second quarter of next year.	11	1
201512	355	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	With the Federal Reserve widely expected to hike interest rates tomorrow, attention has focused on monetary policy divergences across the advanced economies.	11	1
201512	356	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	Policy divergences may present some challenges for US monetary policy.	11	1
201512	357	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	As shown in panel 7, 10-year sovereign yields across the advanced economies remain fairly tightly correlated, suggesting that there is a risk that low yields abroad will put downward pressure on US yields even as the Federal Reserve lifts policy rates.	11	1
201512	358	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	Another consequence of monetary policy divergence has been the sharp appreciation of the dollar against the currencies of other advanced economies.	11	1
201512	359	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	As shown by the red line in panel 8, the jump in the dollar against the AFE currencies over the past two months has been coincident with a rise in the spread between US 24-month-ahead policy rate expectations and expected policy in other advanced economies.	11	1
201512	360	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	Our outlook for the dollar is shown at the top of your next exhibit.	11	1
201512	361	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	We assume that Federal Reserve liftoff has largely been priced into the dollar at this point, and we have penciled in only a touch more appreciation through the first quarter of next year.	11	1
201512	362	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	This forecast is generally consistent with the historical experience associated with periods surrounding the start of previous tightening cycles.	11	1
201512	363	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	As shown by the “butterfly chart” in panel 2, averaging across dollar moves in the 12 months surrounding the past four Federal Reserve tightening cycles (the black line), our forecast dollar path (the dashed red line) is about in line with the average post- tightening trajectory.	11	1
201512	364	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	Of course, we are cognizant of the risk that liftoff might be associated with a more pronounced rise in the dollar, as explored in the “Stronger Dollar” alternative scenario presented in the Tealbook.	11	1
201512	365	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	In this scenario, liftoff and ensuing policy normalization induce a sharp 10 percent further rise in the dollar (shown in panel 3).	11	1
201512	366	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	The stronger dollar pushes down US real net exports and lowers US GDP growth (panel 4) over the next two years, boosting the unemployment rate by about ½ percentage point (panel 5).	11	1
201512	367	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	Another commonly raised concern surrounding liftoff has been the potential for increased financial turbulence in the emerging market economies.	11	1
201512	368	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	However, market movements since the October FOMC meeting suggest that the reaction could be limited.	11	1
201512	369	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	For one, as shown in panel 6, the response of emerging market currencies (the red line) to the sharp increase in US policy rate expectations (the black line) following the October FOMC and October payrolls report was relatively muted.	11	1
201512	370	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	Over the past few months, EME currencies have been more closely correlated with oil prices, which plunged late in the period (the black line in panel 7).	11	1
201512	371	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	We are not sanguine, however, about EME risks, given elevated corporate leverage and falling commodity prices hanging over many emerging market economies.	11	1
201512	372	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	In addition, prospects for China’s exchange rate policy, which roiled emerging markets during the summer, remain a wild card.	11	1
201512	373	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	As shown in panel 8, the renminbi has resumed depreciation this month following a period of relative stability.	11	1
201512	374	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	Our forecast is for the renminbi to remain flat over the next year, as Chinese officials balance concerns for financial stability with a desire to staunch reserve outflows.	11	1
201512	375	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	However, further depreciation is a risk, with the potential to spill over to other emerging markets.	11	1
201512	376	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	Although the staff baseline projection is not premised on significant further appreciation of the broad dollar, the sharp run-up in the dollar since July 2014 continues to weigh heavily on the outlook for US net exports—the subject of your next exhibit.	11	1
201512	377	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	The top two panels of your exhibit provide some detail on how the dollar affects our outlook.	11	1
201512	378	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	The panel on the left shows data and our forecast for real export growth (the solid black line), as well as an estimate from our trade model (the black dots).	11	1
201512	379	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	The model takes foreign GDP and the dollar as its inputs, with the contribution of each of these variables to export growth measured respectively by the green and blue bars in the panel.	11	1
201512	380	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	As shown by the blue bars, the drag due to dollar appreciation is expected to be both large and long lasting, with the peak negative effect not hitting until the first half of next year and the drag lasting into 2018.	11	1
201512	381	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	The dollar also boosts imports, as shown by the blue bars in panel 2, further pulling down the net export contribution to GDP.	11	1
201512	382	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	Here, too, the dollar has large and persistent effects, with the peak boost to imports projected to occur in the first half of next year.	11	1
201512	383	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	Overall, we expect the contribution of net exports to remain negative throughout the forecast, as can be seen in line 3 of the table.	11	1
201512	384	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	Net exports took almost 1 percentage point off US real GDP growth in the first half of 2015 but are estimated to have exerted less drag in the second half, as exports (line 1) remained weak but imports (line 2) slowed as well.	11	1
201512	385	2015-12-16	meeting	GRUBER	Next year, we expect net exports to again weigh heavily on GDP growth, as exports remain about flat while imports shake off some of their second-half weakness.	11	1

201512	447	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	The economic outlook, exhibit 2, the medium- term outlook, real GDP.	12	1
201512	448	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	Looking at potential GDP growth, I was reminded of something I have asked questions about in the past—in 2014, the potential output growth looks like it was quite low.	12	1
201512	449	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	And then I wondered if maybe I hadn’t prepared carefully enough.	12	1
201512	450	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	So I went back to look at the Tealbook chart that has that, and 2014 was buried in an average of 2011 to 2014, which was 1.1 percent.	12	1
201512	451	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	I had sort of forgotten that we have 0.4 here for 2014.	12	1
201512	452	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	I guess the question is— and, John, you are the perfect person, as I understand it, to answer this, since it is based upon your research on Kalman smoothing and things like that.	12	1
201512	453	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	What is the basis for thinking about this?	12	1
201512	454	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	And since it is so amazing, the question really is, does this provide a lesson for the future?	12	1
201512	455	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	Because it is a rather dramatic step-down in potential output growth.	12	1
201512	456	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	If we had found something like that at a period featuring less resource slack, maybe we might think that some inflation will be coming our way.	12	1
201512	457	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	I’m not sure how to think about it.	12	1
201512	458	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	We tried to get the improvement in the output gap right for 2014.	12	1
201512	459	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	Of course, the changing output gap is just the difference between real GDP growth and potential GDP growth.	12	1
201512	460	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	And we saw in 2014 that labor market conditions were improving very rapidly.	12	1
201512	461	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	The unemployment rate was coming down quite a lot, so we thought, “Oh, the output gap must be improving a lot.”	12	1
201512	462	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	So what we essentially did was to say, “Hmm, with GDP growth not as strong as it should be to get that kind of an improvement in the output gap, there must have been some measurement error in the actual GDP numbers.”	12	1
201512	463	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	And because we don’t have room in our accounting system right now for measurement error, we put the measurement error in potential GDP.	12	1
201512	464	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	This is something we are thinking a lot about.	12	1
201512	465	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	In the research of mine that you cite, we do have an explicit role for measurement error, but that isn’t something that’s in our traditional accounting systems.	12	1
201512	466	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	One could imagine a more elaborate system in which you break down real GDP into not just the two components, of potential output and the output gap, but into three components:  potential output, the output gap, and measurement error.	12	1
201512	467	2015-12-16	meeting	ROBERTS	So that’s what’s going on there.	12	1

201512	580	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	I expect real GDP growth over the next two years only somewhat above 2 percent, the unemployment rate at the end of 2017 at 4.6 percent, and a return of PCE inflation to 2 percent by 2018.	13	1

201512	582	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	In summary, a boring forecast, but for a central banker, boring is good.	13	1
201512	583	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	Because my modal forecast is basically more of the same economic outcomes that we have been experiencing over this past year, the mode may not be the most interesting aspect of the outlook.	13	1
201512	584	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	Instead, this may be a good time to consider what could make our modal forecast go wrong.	13	1
201512	585	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	My primary unease with my modal forecast concerns inflation.	13	1
201512	586	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	Core PCE inflation is currently at 1.3 percent.	13	1
201512	587	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	While I’m reasonably confident in my modal forecast based on continued tightening of labor market conditions, an alternative case is not hard to justify.	13	1
201512	588	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	Although the current spread between the core CPI and core PCE is certainly not unprecedented, it is large relative to the spread we’ve experienced over the past five years.	13	1
201512	589	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	If core PCE inflation tended to revert to core CPI inflation, we might be more confident of a return to our 2 percent goal.	13	1
201512	590	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	Unfortunately, that does not seem to be the case.	13	1
201512	591	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	When my staff ran error correction models in the two core series, core CPI tends to converge to core PCE and not the other way around.	13	1
201512	592	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	The implication is that we should not take much solace in the higher value for core CPI inflation.	13	1
201512	593	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	With tighter labor markets, one might expect that surveys and financial market indicators would provide more confidence in the projection of reaching our 2 percent inflation target.	13	1
201512	594	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	However, the SPF PCE median expectation for the next 10 years and the 5-to-10-year-ahead TIPS measures of inflation expectations have recently fallen and now are at or near 10-year lows.	13	1
201512	595	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	The difficulty returning to our inflation target is a global problem.	13	1
201512	596	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	Central banks in developed economies are significantly undershooting their inflation targets.	13	1
201512	597	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	Their attempts to restore inflation to their 2 percent targets have depreciated their currencies against the dollar, a development that is likely to conflict with our own attempts to return to our inflation target.	13	1
201512	598	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	With market expectations tentative and the global low inflation environment potentially inhibiting our own efforts, this is a risk that, if it materializes in coming quarters, could alter my desired monetary policy path.	13	1
201512	599	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	But the risks are not completely asymmetric.	13	1
201512	600	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	The most significant risk that would argue for a tighter monetary policy path than I have in my SEP arises from labor market behavior.	13	1
201512	601	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	Since the onset of the recovery, the labor market has tightened more quickly than I expected.	13	1
201512	602	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	My forecast has real GDP over the next two years averaging close to 2 percent, not much different than what we have averaged over the past several years.	13	1
201512	603	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	However, despite very modest and slower-than-expected growth, the unemployment rate over the past several years has fallen more than expected.	13	1
201512	604	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	Compounding that risk, we also do not have a particularly good record of stabilizing the unemployment rate at its natural rate.	13	1
201512	605	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	Instead, monetary policy often contributes to a significant undershooting of our estimates of the natural rate of unemployment.	13	1
201512	606	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	This risk is mitigated somewhat by the expectation that, as in the Tealbook, some workers will be drawn back into the labor force, so that some of the remaining labor market slack not captured in the U- 3 rate will diminish.	13	1
201512	607	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	But a plausible alternative is that the unemployment rate falls well below our estimate of the natural rate of unemployment.	13	1
201512	608	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	I’m not deeply concerned that such undershooting will cause a sharp rise in inflation, but rather that our attempts to return unemployment to the natural rate will similarly result in overshooting, above the natural rate, setting off a cycle of corrections that might induce additional volatility into the economy.	13	1
201512	609	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	I am perhaps less concerned about undershooting and overshooting than I would be if I held to the Tealbook’s natural rate of unemployment estimate, as my current estimate of the natural rate of unemployment is 4.7 percent.	13	1
201512	610	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	This is starting to represent a sizable difference from the staff’s forecast.	13	1
201512	611	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	But even with a much lower natural rate, if the estimate were significantly surpassed, I would become more worried about future inflationary pressures and about inadvertently creating another recession in our attempts to avoid such pressures.	13	1
201512	612	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	In such a context, I might want a tighter normalization path to avoid such a scenario.	13	1
201512	613	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	Finally, I do not see any imminent threat to financial stability.	13	1
201512	614	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	However, as outlined in the Chair’s recent e-mail, overall financial conditions might be conducive to sowing the seeds of such problems.	13	1
201512	615	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	While macroprudential tools may be the preferred first line of defense, I have concerns about whether we have sufficient foresight, tools, and political will to use those tools to full effect.	13	1
201512	616	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	To be sure, we also do not know how effective monetary policy would be in slowing particular activity that might lead to financial instability.	13	1
201512	617	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	But we certainly have the ability to implement standard monetary policy tools if we deem them necessary and effective.	13	1
201512	618	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thus, I am probably more willing to lean on monetary policy tools than some others, at least until I have more confidence in the use of macroprudential tools.	13	1
201512	619	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	I am glad that we are having a more fulsome discussion in April, but at least for me a buildup of financial-stability pressures might influence how quickly I would be willing to normalize.	13	1
201512	620	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	My baseline forecast at this time is that those concerns will not rise to the level that would alter my preferred path of the short-term interest rate, but monitoring financial conditions closely in coming quarters is certainly warranted.	13	1
