201512	633	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	Lower natural gas prices have resulted in reduced drilling activity in the Marcellus region.	13	1
201512	634	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	Pipeline construction to connect existing wells is still active, however.	13	1
201512	635	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	Residential real estate markets continued to improve at a moderate pace.	13	1
201512	636	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	We hear that some homebuyers are entering the market anticipating rate increases ahead, but shortages of buildable lots and labor are said to be driving up costs and limiting single-family construction activity.	13	1
201512	637	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	Our bankers say that demand for credit is growing and credit quality is improving, but competition is still fierce for good borrowers.	13	1
201512	638	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	They say that TRID, the new closing document requirement, is increasing mortgage origination costs, and that it is going to be difficult for small community banks to afford to do any mortgage lending.	13	1
201512	639	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	The struggle to find qualified workers continues across a range of occupations.	13	1
201512	640	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	My favorite anecdote this time is that construction companies are posting armed guards at work sites to discourage the poaching of construction crews.	13	1
201512	641	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	And, finally, in the category of “be careful what you wish for,” we hear of sizable hiring plans at large D.C. law firms.	13	1
201512	642	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	Turning to the national economy, I agree with the Tealbook’s assessment that the outlook has not changed much since our previous meeting.	13	1
201512	643	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	I’ll touch on just a few significant developments.	13	1
201512	644	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	First, consumer spending is obviously the key to the outlook.	13	1
201512	645	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	Although the reports on real PCE were weak in September and October, there were quirks each month that reduced their signal value, and retail sales ex gasoline were up significantly in November.	13	1
201512	646	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	I expect consumer spending to continue to grow at around 3 percent for at least another year, bolstered by strong income growth, good job prospects, and a solid household balance sheet.	13	1
201512	647	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	Second, we are seeing some signs of increasing wage growth in the data, and that fits well with the many reports we have seen about shortages of skilled workers and growing wage pressures.	13	1
201512	648	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	It seems plausible now that we will see a pickup in wage gains next year, something that should support a healthy household sector.	13	1
201512	649	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	Third, the federal budget agreement should provide a direct boost to overall economic activity next year.	13	1
201512	650	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	Not only does it add to outlays in the near term, but, as I said, some firms in our District report that it reduces uncertainty, a development that should itself encourage spending.	13	1
201512	651	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	One source of concern of late is that manufacturing diffusion indexes have been noticeably soft, including our own Fifth District index.	13	1
201512	652	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	At the same time, though, the Board’s industrial production index for manufacturing as a whole has been rising at a modest pace.	13	1
201512	653	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	Thinking about how those two types of sources aggregate disparate sectors, I am more confident in the Board’s index, so I share the staff’s view that total manufacturing output should continue to advance even in the face of further strength in the dollar.	13	1
201512	654	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	In sum, recent developments line up well with the Tealbook’s forecast of above-trend real GDP growth next year.	13	1
201512	655	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	I wrote down 2.4 percent, which is not that far from the Tealbook.	13	1
201512	656	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	I part company with the staff a bit on the near-term inflation outlook, however.	13	1
201512	657	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	In the absence of shocks, I think it is reasonable to look for headline and core inflation to make substantial progress toward 2 percent next year.	13	1
201512	658	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	In any case, there is substantial uncertainty about the inflation outlook over the next two years, and we need to keep this in mind as we craft language on policy guidance.	13	1
201512	659	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	Thank you.	13	1
201512	660	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	13	1
201512	661	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	President George.	13	1
201512	662	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201512	663	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	The declines in energy prices and farm incomes continue to weigh heavily on the Tenth District economy.	13	1
201512	664	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	Oil prices have retreated further since our previous meeting, and our industry contacts now expect oil prices to remain depressed or to drop even further in the first half of 2016 before recovering somewhat in the second half.	13	1
201512	665	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	As a result, another round of steep capital spending cuts and associated layoffs are expected.	13	1
201512	666	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	Several District energy firms also have had their credit downgraded further in recent weeks, and contacts expect more consolidation and defaults in 2016.	13	1
201512	667	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	Headwinds due to supply and demand factors have also created a more pessimistic outlook for farm income since the previous meeting.	13	1
201512	668	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	Crop prices remain 10 percent below year- ago levels, and we are approximately 35 percent below the five-year average following reports of near-record domestic production.	13	1
201512	669	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	Additionally, cattle prices have fallen.	13	1
201512	670	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	Little improvement is expected in the near term, as global demand for US agricultural and food exports has declined in 2015 about 10 percent as a result of the strong dollar and increased competition from other major agricultural and food exporters.	13	1
201512	671	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	Our District manufacturing survey has slipped back below the breakeven level of 50 after two months of showing signs of stabilizing.	13	1
201512	672	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	Activity is lowest in Oklahoma, but even less energy-intensive states are showing some signs of softening.	13	1
201512	673	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	Despite the headwinds arising from commodity price behavior, we continue to see strength in other areas.	13	1
201512	674	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	Based on our surveys, the strongest employment gains are expected in the high-tech services and transportation sectors.	13	1
201512	675	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	Some employment gains are also expected in the real estate sector as home prices continue to appreciate across the District and home inventory levels remain low.	13	1
201512	676	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	For the national economy, I expect growth of around 2 percent in 2015 despite notable drags due to weakness in net exports and lower investment in the energy sector.	13	1
201512	677	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	Looking ahead, my forecast is for growth of 2½ percent next year, as global growth is expected to be modestly higher than this year and the headwinds generated by a high foreign exchange value of the dollar begin to wane.	13	1
201512	678	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	Conditions generally look favorable for solid consumption growth.	13	1
201512	679	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	As household balance sheets have improved, the savings rate is high compared with the past few years.	13	1
201512	680	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	House prices are rising, wage growth is showing some signs of improving, and gasoline prices are low.	13	1
201512	681	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	Even so, it is worth considering how much more headroom consumers may have, especially given the brisk pace of auto sales.	13	1
201512	682	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	Durable consumption has historically been about 12 percent of total consumption following recessions and then rises to about 14 percent as an expansion matures.	13	1
201512	683	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	Currently, durables represent about 11 percent of total consumption, suggesting, perhaps, that some upside potential exists in terms of durable goods consumption.	13	1
201512	684	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	Also, I have noted that the average age of durable goods remains somewhat high compared with before the crisis.	13	1
201512	685	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	My forecast for the unemployment rate relies on some further improvement in the labor market, although the decline in participation of prime-age males seems unlikely to substantially reverse.	13	1
201512	686	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	In 2010, 14 percent of prime-age males hadn’t worked within the past year.	13	1
201512	687	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	This percentage is virtually unchanged today.	13	1
201512	688	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	In contrast, from 2010 to 2015, the share of these detached workers who haven’t worked in the past five years increased from 50 percent to 61 percent.	13	1
201512	689	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	The rise in detachment during a period of labor market improvement suggests that deeper structural obstacles exist that may not be easily overcome by a cyclical improvement in labor market conditions.	13	1
201512	690	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	In terms of wages, we are seeing some signs of faster wage growth after controlling for compositional effects.	13	1
201512	691	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	For example, using the Current Population Survey, the Federal Reserve Bank of Atlanta wage tracker follows individual workers and shows that average annual wages have increased from less than 2 percent in 2010 to about 3½ percent for prime-age workers.	13	1
201512	692	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	Along these same lines, the latest NFIB survey shows a sharp increase in the number of firms planning to raise wages.	13	1
201512	693	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	Turning to inflation, there have been considerable disinflationary pressures generated by the commodity price decline and dollar appreciation over the past year.	13	1
201512	694	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	From the third quarter of last year to the third quarter of this year, WTI prices fell 52 percent, more than they have ever fallen in periods other than postwar US recessions.	13	1
201512	695	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	Over this period, the foreign exchange value of the dollar, of course, has also sharply appreciated.	13	1
201512	696	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	My staff estimates that the simultaneous drag generated by these outsized movements in both commodity prices and the dollar are subtracting about 45 basis points from core PCE inflation, an estimate that is similar to what the Chair reported in a recent speech but using a somewhat different approach.	13	1
201512	697	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	Without these headwinds, core inflation looks to be running at almost 1¾ percent.	13	1
201512	698	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	Another factor that supports my confidence that inflation will rise is the stability of long- term survey-based inflation expectations.	13	1
201512	699	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	My own preferred survey measure is the five-year, five-year-ahead forecast of PCE inflation.	13	1
201512	700	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	This measure edged up to 2.1 percent from 2 percent in the first half of this year and has since remained relatively stable.	13	1
201512	701	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	Although the University of Michigan survey of longer-term inflation expectations has edged down, this survey appears to be more sensitive to the drop in gasoline prices and is not necessarily a sign that longer-term inflation expectations have declined to a level inconsistent with our 2 percent goal.	13	1
201512	702	2015-12-16	meeting	GEORGE	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1

201512	704	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	President Lockhart.	13	1
201512	705	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201512	706	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	As a final sounding of my District’s contacts before the possible liftoff decision at this meeting, my team met with a large number of business leaders across the Sixth District.	13	1
201512	707	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	The spread of interviews was fairly representative of the national industrial mix.	13	1
201512	708	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	Businesses appear to be ready for and supportive of a rate increase coming from this meeting.	13	1
201512	709	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	This support seemed to be based on a broadly held view that business activity is expanding at more or less the same moderate pace that we’ve seen for most of the recovery.	13	1
201512	710	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	Overall, I would characterize the outlook of the majority of our contacts as “restrained optimism.”	13	1
201512	711	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	Major employers indicated that demand for workers continues to grow, and wage growth appears to be firming.	13	1
201512	712	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	Pockets of softness were reported, as expected, in regions and industries with concentrations in oil exploration and refining.	13	1
201512	713	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	Companies with significant ties to commodity production also reported slowing, as did some manufacturing firms.	13	1
201512	714	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	Continuing heightened inventory levels were mentioned frequently as a potential source of production weakness in the near term.	13	1
201512	715	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	This contrasts somewhat with the Tealbook’s more benign view of the inventory situation.	13	1
201512	716	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	Even in the auto industry, whose sales are very strong, we heard concern about inventory trends.	13	1
201512	717	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	Our director, who heads the nation’s largest auto retailer, mentioned a recent surge in inventories partially fueled by imports.	13	1
201512	718	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	Apparently, auto manufacturers with global operations had been redirecting shipments to the United States as the market they consider as having the best prospects for excess global inventory absorption.	13	1
201512	719	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	He offered the opinion that, in the near term, the pace of sales can absorb the heightened inventories, but he expressed concern about whether the historic high sales pace is sustainable.	13	1
201512	720	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	Although earlier in the year we heard references to logistics bottlenecks—most prominently the Long Beach port strike—as contributing to the inventory buildup.	13	1
201512	721	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	In this cycle, we heard more emphasis on disappointing sales.	13	1
201512	722	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	In that regard, consumer spending reports were mixed.	13	1
201512	723	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	Several contacts said they expect significant price discounting in coming weeks to move unsold stocks.	13	1
201512	724	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	Regarding business investment, our chair, who participates in the Business Roundtable, noted a downshift in the composite business outlook of the group and, with that, a sharp reduction in anticipated capital expenditures over the next six months.	13	1
201512	725	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	Despite some concerns, most of our contacts are expecting continued moderate expansion of business activities.	13	1
201512	726	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	They are seeing the glass as half full.	13	1
201512	727	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	Along with their support for liftoff, we heard broad support for taking a cautious approach to the pace of normalization until underlying points of strength in business conditions can be confirmed.	13	1
201512	728	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	In my outlook for the US economy, I’ve lowered my forecast of near-term real GDP growth a little, in order to reflect the cautious sentiment we detected along with the mixed data picture.	13	1
201512	729	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	This puts my growth outlook pretty much into line with this meeting’s Tealbook forecast.	13	1
201512	730	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	I’ve also lowered our projection of headline inflation for 2016, as has the Tealbook.	13	1
201512	731	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	We recently surveyed businesses once again about their “business-input inflation” expectations.	13	1
201512	732	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	While cost expectations of firms are more or less unchanged from earlier surveys, we picked up notable differences in perspective from industry to industry.	13	1
201512	733	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	Our data on businesses in the retail industry and manufacturing showed slippage in year-ahead cost expectations compared with this time last year.	13	1
201512	734	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	We’re not prepared to conclude that these moves are an early signal of a more broadly based downshift in inflation expectations of businesses, but they may be an additional cautionary note regarding inflation expectations.	13	1
201512	735	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	In updating my forecast for this meeting’s SEP submission, the trend of inflation expectation readings was hard to ignore.	13	1
201512	736	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	Six months ago, we were getting different readings from financial markets and household surveys.	13	1
201512	737	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	Now, it’s my sense that the various indicators of inflation expectations are more in alignment, and so it’s a little harder to claim that expectations remain anchored at levels near the Committee’s target.	13	1
201512	738	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	In my projections for 2016, even as I’ve lowered my estimate of headline inflation, I’m treating recently softening inflation expectations as representing a risk to the outlook.	13	1
201512	739	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	Consistent with that treatment, my balance of risk perspective has the risks to growth and employment as balanced, while I have inflation risks showing a downside bias.	13	1
201512	740	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1

201512	742	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	President Bullard.	13	1
201512	743	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201512	744	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	Information received from District contacts since the previous FOMC meeting suggests that overall economic conditions continue to improve at a modest pace.	13	1
201512	745	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	Results from our business outlook survey in the District were consistent with improving conditions but did not show signs of accelerating growth.	13	1
201512	746	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	Preliminary District employment data through October have been stronger than in previous months and consistent with modest job growth.	13	1
201512	747	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	Two notable business developments in the District were Ford’s $1.3 billion investment in the Louisville Ford truck plant and St Jude Medical’s announcement of a $9 billion investment in Memphis.	13	1
201512	748	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	Each project is estimated to bring about 2,000 jobs to the local area.	13	1
201512	749	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	The unemployment rate in the District measured across metropolitan statistical areas is 4.9 percent based on the latest reading, just below the current national unemployment rate and consistent with the Committee’s median view of the long-run rate of unemployment for the nation.	13	1
201512	750	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	Anecdotal information received from District hiring managers continues to suggest building wage pressures.	13	1
201512	751	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	Comments from directors across a variety of industries suggest that 2016 wage pools are being set to produce wage increases of about 3 percent—that’s in a world of low inflation and low productivity growth.	13	1
201512	752	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	Nationally, the strong real GDP growth registered in the second quarter of 2015 does not appear to be carrying over into the second half of the year.	13	1
201512	753	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	The evolving data, as well as the consensus of most forecasters, suggest that the moderate growth and low inflation registered in the third quarter will carry into the fourth quarter.	13	1
201512	754	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	Indeed, the average of the Federal Reserve Bank of St Louis’s three nowcasts is 2.3 percent real GDP growth in the fourth quarter.	13	1
201512	755	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	In short, real GDP growth during the second half of 2015 has not materialized as we in St Louis expected.	13	1
201512	756	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	Accordingly, we have reduced our growth expectations further, and we now stand at a real GDP growth forecast broadly similar to private forecasters for 2016, around 2¾ percent.	13	1
201512	757	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	Concerning unemployment, we have been more optimistic than the median of this Committee and, hence, more accurate during the past three years.	13	1
201512	758	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	We continue to be more optimistic and have penciled in a 4.3 percent unemployment rate for the end of 2016.	13	1
201512	759	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	We think this is very reasonable provided growth comes in at 2½ to 3 percent for 2016.	13	1
201512	760	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	This forecast is more aggressive than the Tealbook and most private forecasters, but most forecasters have underestimated the pace of improvement in labor market outcomes over the past several years.	13	1
201512	761	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	Should job gains continue to average 200,000 a month, this would be far above the pace necessary to keep the unemployment rate constant.	13	1
201512	762	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	Accordingly, we think the unemployment rate is likely to continue to fall in 2016.	13	1
201512	763	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	Domestic inflation readings continue to be difficult to interpret as a result of continuing turmoil in international energy and commodities markets.	13	1
201512	764	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	We have been expecting oil prices to stabilize and that, given the current pace of increase in other prices, headline inflation would return to target rather mechanically during 2016.	13	1
201512	765	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	This is still our baseline, but further declines in crude oil prices in recent days bear careful watching.	13	1
201512	766	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	I continue to see lower crude oil prices as a bullish factor for the US economy, as I think it is inconsistent to argue that it’s both a negative factor when oil prices go up and when they go down.	13	1
201512	767	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	We have to choose one or the other.	13	1
201512	768	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	I think having lower oil prices is a bullish factor for the US economy.	13	1
201512	769	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	Nevertheless, renewed oil price declines may delay the return of headline inflation to target.	13	1
201512	770	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	We have, accordingly, moderated our inflation forecast in the current SEP round.	13	1
201512	771	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	We still expect a modest overshooting of the Committee’s inflation target, with headline PCE inflation peaking at 2.1 percent year over year by the end of 2016 and stabilizing at 2 percent thereafter, provided this Committee pursues the appropriate level of policy accommodation over the forecast horizon.	13	1
201512	772	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	The extent of this overshooting has been tempered relative to previous forecasts and, in addition, has been pushed further into the future.	13	1
201512	773	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	I see recent oil price declines as a downside risk to this inflation forecast, but I’m not willing to adjust the forecast further on the basis of the information available as of today.	13	1
201512	774	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	Our current inflation forecast is now closer to the SPF forecast than it has been but above the Tealbook.	13	1
201512	775	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	Again, I think this is reasonable provided that growth comes in at 2½ to 3 percent in 2016 and unemployment falls below 4½ percent.	13	1
201512	776	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	Considering underlying measures of inflation, I continue to think that our so-called core inflation is not the right measure and that continued focus on this is doing a disservice to US monetary policy.	13	1
201512	777	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	As Governor Fischer and, just now, President George and many others have pointed out, in the current episode of dramatic crude oil price declines, core inflation, despite the exclusion of food and energy prices, has still been importantly affected by the large energy price movement, enough to take several tenths off the year-over-year inflation rate.	13	1
201512	778	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	Better measures of underlying trend inflation are available and should assume more prominence in the Committee’s decisionmaking.	13	1
201512	779	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	A possible contender is the Federal Reserve Bank of Dallas’s trimmed mean PCE inflation rate, which is currently running at 1.7 percent year over year.	13	1
201512	780	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	This is only three-tenths below the Committee’s goal and is likely to rise gradually over the forecast horizon.	13	1
201512	781	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	This suggests that the Committee’s inflation goal is close to being met.	13	1
201512	782	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	Another possibility would be the so-called sticky-price CPI, which came up today, at 2.4 percent year over year.	13	1
201512	783	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	The sticky-price CPI has the advantage of theoretical backing in the New Keynesian literature, which says that it’s the sticky prices you should worry about in an economy in which sticky prices are the key friction.	13	1
201512	784	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	New Keynesian ideas influence a lot of the thinking around this table.	13	1
201512	785	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	Inflation expectations have continued to deteriorate, and this is a concern to me, but these declines remain closely correlated with movements in global dollar oil prices and perhaps cannot be interpreted in a straightforward way at the current juncture.	13	1
201512	786	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	For this reason, I remain in a wait-and-see mode with respect to measures of inflation expectations.	13	1
201512	787	2015-12-16	meeting	BULLARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201512	788	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	13	1

201512	796	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	Overall, I would continue to categorize growth in the Third District as modest.	13	1
201512	797	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	Looking at employment growth in a bit more detail:  October jobs data were strong in both New Jersey and Pennsylvania, with most of the growth concentrated in service-sector jobs.	13	1
201512	798	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	Employment growth has now accelerated to the national average, and participation rates have stabilized at around 62.9 percent.	13	1
201512	799	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	Employment in mining and drilling has declined over the past three months but is still up year over year.	13	1
201512	800	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	Notably, the tristate unemployment rate declined three-tenths of a percent in October to 5.2 percent.	13	1
201512	801	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	One interesting feature of the labor market in my region is that Delaware is experiencing a persistent increase in labor force growth driven in part by the reentry of workers into the labor force.	13	1
201512	802	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	I don’t know whether this behavior will remain special to Delaware or prove to be a harbinger of a more general labor market development, but it’s worth noting that Delaware has proven to be a first state in at least one other historically significant event—go Blue Hens.	13	1
201512	803	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	Indicators of Third District manufacturing activity continue to indicate weakness.	13	1
201512	804	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	The current activity index in our December Manufacturing Business Outlook Survey, which will be released Thursday morning, came in at minus 5.9, down from 1.9 in November—indicating that activity is slightly negative, a condition that’s now prevailed for the past four months.	13	1
201512	805	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	We did see a pickup in shipments, but it was ever so slight.	13	1
201512	806	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	However, indicators of future activity, although still solidly in positive territory, declined significantly from 43.4 to 23.0, and that number is now slightly below its nonrecessionary average.	13	1
201512	807	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	On the other hand, activity in the service sector remains robust.	13	1
201512	808	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	In our nonmanufacturing business survey, the general activity index in November remained close to its nonrecessionary average, coming in at 26.3, down somewhat from its October reading.	13	1
201512	809	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	Respondents remain upbeat, with the future activity indexes remaining solidly in positive territory.	13	1
201512	810	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	An initial report received from a contact regarding activity on Black Friday indicated that crowd volumes were higher than they had seen in several years and that shoppers were socializing less, were more focused on shopping, and were handling multiple bags of merchandise.	13	1
201512	811	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	Subsequent reports of holiday shopping activity in the District have been somewhat mixed.	13	1
201512	812	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	However, auto dealers are reporting brisk sales, and one executive indicated that consumers are using the fall in gas prices to upgrade the class of vehicles they are buying.	13	1
201512	813	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	This behavior was particularly influencing sales of larger SUVs.	13	1
201512	814	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	In real estate, housing and construction are showing modest improvements largely driven by the growth in multifamily housing units.	13	1
201512	815	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	The single-family housing sector of the market remains lackluster, and house price appreciation in the region lags that of the nation.	13	1
201512	816	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	In the pricing arena, there appear to be distinct differences across sectors.	13	1
201512	817	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	In manufacturing there is very little evidence of price pressures, with the indexes for both prices received and paid coming in negative in the December Manufacturing Business Outlook Survey.	13	1
201512	818	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	The opposite was true in the nonmanufacturing survey, with the analogous indexes experiencing increases that accelerated somewhat in November.	13	1
201512	819	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	This dichotomy carried over into our inaugural firm price expectation survey, which measured next-year price forecasts for own prices, compensation, and overall inflation.	13	1
201512	820	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	The median forecast among manufacturers was for their own prices to rise 1 percent in the fourth quarter of next year compared with the prices they charge this quarter, while the comparable forecast for nonmanufacturers was 3 percent.	13	1
201512	821	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	Regarding total compensation, the median expected change for both sets of respondents was an increase of 3 percent, and both groups anticipated that consumer inflation would rise 2 percent fourth quarter over fourth quarter.	13	1
201512	822	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	However, although wages are expected to rise at a somewhat faster pace for selected skills, few firms will be increasing wages at a significant pace for all workers.	13	1
201512	823	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	Also, a much larger fraction of firms are reporting difficulty finding workers with the required skills compared with six months ago.	13	1
201512	824	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	Turning to the nation as a whole, I believe that the real economy remains healthy.	13	1
201512	825	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	My forecast is for the economy to grow at 2.2 percent in 2015, accelerating a bit to 2.5 percent in 2016, then growing at 2.4 percent and 2.3 percent in 2017 and 2018, respectively.	13	1
201512	826	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	I see Q4 unemployment at 5 percent, but I see the rate dipping to 4.8 percent in 2016 before gradually rising to 5.0 percent in 2018.	13	1
201512	827	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	With regard to inflation, I see both headline and core measures gradually returning to target.	13	1
201512	828	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	Next year, I foresee a considerable bounceback in inflation as the effects of falling oil prices and dollar appreciation dissipate.	13	1
201512	829	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	I anticipate that headline PCE inflation will be 1.6 percent in 2016 and reach our target by 2018, and that core PCE inflation will be 1.7 percent next year and will not reach target until sometime in 2018.	13	1
201512	830	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	Thus, my forecast is a tad weaker on unemployment and slightly more optimistic on growth than the Board staff’s forecast in the Tealbook, but generally the overall contour is not appreciably different, at least in any meaningful statistical sense.	13	1
201512	831	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	The last comment I’d like to make as we approach liftoff is that I’d like to raise concerns with respect to the phrase “data dependency.”	13	1
201512	832	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	Although the Committee has been careful to emphasize that it is the trend in data, not any one data point, that matters in forming policy, this is, as we know, oftentimes overlooked by the media and the public.	13	1
201512	833	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	In particular, over the recent past, there has been a tendency for Q1 data to come in on the weak side perhaps as a result of residual seasonality.	13	1
201512	834	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	As we go forward, I believe it will be important to look at the data very broadly as we interpret and publicly discuss the consequences of our actions.	13	1
201512	835	2015-12-16	meeting	HARKER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1

201512	843	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201512	844	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	The tone of my discussions with business leaders this time was cautious to downright pessimistic, but perhaps this reflects their industrial mix.	13	1
201512	845	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	I talked to a number of manufacturers with big international exposures.	13	1
201512	846	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	Conditions are particularly bad in the steel industry.	13	1
201512	847	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	Prices of some of their benchmark products are down about 40 percent from a year ago, and one of my directors mentioned that a couple of large firms may be in serious financial trouble.	13	1
201512	848	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	The heavy equipment manufacturers remain quite downbeat and for some time have been laying off workers in response to persistent low demand for mining and agricultural equipment.	13	1
201512	849	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	My steel and heavy equipment contacts did hope to see a pickup in demand for construction-related inputs and machinery in the spring and noted that the highway bill should help.	13	1
201512	850	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	I guess this is another Federal Reserve stimulus program.	13	1
201512	851	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	[Laughter]	13	1
201512	852	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	Looking ahead, manufacturers and my other contacts with global business presence generally see Western Europe coming off the bottom.	13	1
201512	853	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	China should either stabilize or pick up in part as a result of recent fiscal measures there, and South America, particularly Brazil, is expected to remain a mess.	13	1
201512	854	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	The bright spot in my District is the auto industry.	13	1
201512	855	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	Of course, sales have been quite strong the past few months, and Ford, for one, is expecting only a modest slowdown in 2016 from the industry’s recent pace.	13	1
201512	856	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	Their forecast is premised on only a gradual tightening in financial conditions.	13	1
201512	857	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	Something more rapid would likely hit car payments in a big enough way that consumers would delay purchases or buy less-expensive models.	13	1
201512	858	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	Outside the auto area, the news about the consumer has been okay but not robust.	13	1
201512	859	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	For example, my director from Discover credit cards reported just moderate increases in sales and credit usage.	13	1
201512	860	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	With regard to wages and prices, a number of my directors reported wage gains, but these were largely for upper- and some lower-tiered workers.	13	1
201512	861	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	The segment in the middle continues to miss out.	13	1
201512	862	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	Ford characterized the UAW contracts as a bit expensive on wages and bonuses.	13	1
201512	863	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	They expected some higher wage spillover upstream to parts suppliers.	13	1
201512	864	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	However, in return for higher payouts, Ford will receive some offsetting productivity-enhancing changes in work rules.	13	1
201512	865	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	Outside these few wage reports, I’ve not heard a thing about cost pressures or increasing prices.	13	1
201512	866	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	In financial markets, our contacts’ basic message was that credit conditions have tightened somewhat since the previous FOMC meeting, and here I should mention that all of our calls were made before last week’s problems in high-yield markets.	13	1
201512	867	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	Of course, our contacts noted that spreads are up, and they’ve risen more since then.	13	1
201512	868	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	They attributed these earlier increases in part to a reduction of liquidity in corporate bonds and asset-backed securities, but mostly the increases seemed to reflect repricing of high-yield debt, especially debt rated triple-C and below.	13	1
201512	869	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	We also heard of somewhat tighter credit conditions in commercial real estate, especially for new construction loans, and there most notably in the multifamily sector.	13	1
201512	870	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	Overall, as of last week, our contacts’ perception was that we are seeing a healthy repricing of riskier assets and not an unwarranted reduction in credit availability.	13	1
201512	871	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	One caveat with regard to this assessment is that our small business financing contact at PayNet noted a sharp drop in their small business lending index in October.	13	1
201512	872	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	This seems like something to keep an eye on.	13	1
201512	873	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	After all, as my large corporate contacts tell me they are either maintaining employment levels or laying off workers, I have been speculating that small and medium-size enterprises are currently a source of strength nationally.	13	1
201512	874	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	Turning to the national outlook, on balance, the incoming data on spending have been a bit softer than we projected in our September SEP submission.	13	1
201512	875	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	We’ve lowered our forecast of growth by a few tenths over the next year or so.	13	1
201512	876	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	We now see GDP growth averaging in the 2¼ to 2½ percent range over the projection period.	13	1
201512	877	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	Although this is faster than the Tealbook, our assumptions regarding potential GDP growth also were a few tenths higher.	13	1
201512	878	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	We see resource gaps closing in 2017 and then the economy running only a bit above potential in 2018.	13	1
201512	879	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	So my outlook does not have output overshooting potential to the same degree as the Tealbook.	13	1
201512	880	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	We made no material changes to our inflation forecast.	13	1
201512	881	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	It looks similar to the Tealbook, with inflation slowly moving up close to target by the end of the projection period.	13	1
201512	882	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	I did want to note President Bullard’s comment about core inflation rates and trimmed mean PCE—I have not studied this carefully, but my staff had looked at the average inflation experience over some longer period of time.	13	1
201512	883	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	For the period from 1984 to the present, trimmed mean PCE inflation is about two-tenths higher than both total PCE and core PCE inflation, which are exactly 2.3 percent, on average, over that time period.	13	1
201512	884	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	So there quite likely could be some wedge in there, and at least over that longer period of time, it was higher.	13	1
201512	885	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	It’s something to keep in mind, as it’s higher than our target inflation rate measured by the increase in total PCE prices.	13	1
201512	886	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	My forecast is predicated on the key assumption that policy rates rise at a very gradual pace and that the Committee strongly communicates its state-dependent expectation that rates will follow such a gradual path.	13	1
201512	887	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	FOMC communications should also make clear the Committee’s strong commitment to a symmetric 2 percent inflation target.	13	1
201512	888	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	We should actively disabuse the public of any wrong impression that 2 percent is a ceiling.	13	1
201512	889	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	Reaffirming our symmetric objective would solidify the upward pull on actual inflation from inflationary expectations.	13	1
201512	890	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	Without this commitment to symmetry, our Federal Reserve Bank of Chicago outlook would not be projecting inflation to rise to target over the forecast period.	13	1
201512	891	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	I will also note that, largely to better reflect the reality of our Committee communications, I changed my policy rate assumptions in the SEP to have liftoff occurring tomorrow instead of in June 2016.	13	1
201512	892	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	My policy assumption includes only two moves next year and then about 100 basis point increases in both 2017 and 2018.	13	1
201512	893	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	This policy rate path is premised on the assumption that by late next year, core inflation will finally be making some visible progress toward target and real economic activity will have continued to grow moderately above trend.	13	1
201512	894	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	These developments should give us more confidence that the equilibrium real interest rate is moving up as well.	13	1
201512	895	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	This is a crucial state-dependent feature of my overall economic projection.	13	1
201512	896	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	If we do not reach these data markers next year, then I would find it necessary to reassess the policy rate path needed to achieve our dual-mandate goals.	13	1
201512	897	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	And I believe we should clearly communicate such state dependence now.	13	1
201512	898	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	The public needs clear guidance beyond our decision tomorrow.	13	1

201512	901	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Brainard.	13	1
201512	902	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Thank you.	13	1
201512	903	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	I have been very encouraged by recent labor market developments.	13	1
201512	904	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Robust job gains in October and November have brought average monthly employment growth for the year to 210,000, bringing moderate further increases in resource utilization.	13	1
201512	905	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	And the continued subdued rates of nominal wage growth suggest some further slack may remain.	13	1
201512	906	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Among the various measures of nominal wage growth, the ECI provides the best overall measure.	13	1
201512	907	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	It is comprehensive in terms of the types of compensation it includes, representative of the “universe” of firms, and the least subject to shifts in the industry and occupation of workers.	13	1
201512	908	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	The ECI measure increased only 1.9 percent over the 12 months ending in September, little different from the average pace of increase over the recovery.	13	1
201512	909	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Similarly, the most recent 12-month gain in average hourly earnings, at 2.3 percent, is only slightly above this average pace.	13	1
201512	910	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	In contrast, compensation per hour in the business sector rose 3½ percent over the past year, a substantial step-up from the preceding year.	13	1
201512	911	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	However, this series is quite volatile, and its previous history suggests that rates of increase should move lower in the period ahead.	13	1
201512	912	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	With overall unemployment already low at 5 percent, the continuing subdued rate of wage gains naturally raises the question, where are the margins of remaining slack?	13	1
201512	913	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	In this regard, a number of labor market experts have noted that the employment-to-population ratio for 25- to 54-year-olds remains 2½ percentage points below its average level in 2007 and is only halfway back to its level before the recession.	13	1
201512	914	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Most of the shortfall reflects lower rates of labor force participation.	13	1
201512	915	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Of course, it is difficult to judge the extent to which secular or cyclical forces are depressing the participation rate for this group, but several factors suggest that at least some portion of this shortfall may be cyclical.	13	1
201512	916	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	First, historically, employment rates for this group have been quite high, close to 90 percent for men and over 70 percent for women, suggesting a strong desire for employment among this age group.	13	1
201512	917	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Second, individuals out of the labor force tend to respond to any improvement in labor market conditions with a lag because of transition costs of moving to employment from other activities such as schooling or child care.	13	1
201512	918	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	So recovery along this margin could reasonably be expected to lag conditions in the labor market.	13	1
201512	919	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	In addition, gauges of the attractiveness of the labor market, such as job finding rates, quits rates, and wages, have improved more slowly than the unemployment rate, holding out hope that there is room for further improvements in those conditions to attract workers back into the labor force.	13	1
201512	920	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Finally, the share of employees working part time for economic reasons, at 4 percent, also remains about 1 percentage point above pre-recession norms.	13	1
201512	921	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Again, although some of this higher level may be due to structural changes, some portion may reflect a cyclical shortfall.	13	1
201512	922	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Along with this encouraging improvement in the labor market, domestic demand continues to increase at a moderate pace.	13	1
201512	923	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	The recent data on consumer spending have been close to expectations—with auto sales, in particular, remaining strong—and real PCE looks to increase nearly 3 percent this year, similar to last year’s pace and up noticeably from earlier in the recovery.	13	1
201512	924	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Nonetheless, some of the supports for consumer spending are likely to moderate or diminish in the period ahead.	13	1
201512	925	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	For instance, asset prices have reached or exceeded gauges of historical levels, so future gains in wealth will likely be more moderate than earlier in the recovery.	13	1
201512	926	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Similarly, credit conditions have mostly normalized.	13	1
201512	927	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	In short, the strength in consumer spending over the medium term is likely to depend on further improvement in the labor market and, in particular, on a pickup in wage growth.	13	1
201512	928	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	In addition, government purchases are likely to increase somewhat next year, given the recently passed bipartisan Budget Act.	13	1
201512	929	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	But even with this boost, the contribution of government purchases to aggregate demand will remain relatively modest.	13	1
201512	930	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	In contrast to consumption, private fixed investment has decelerated from earlier in the recovery as pent-up demand for capital has waned.	13	1
201512	931	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Most recently, weakness in the energy sector has weighed on investment.	13	1
201512	932	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	And with the recent step-down in oil prices, this weakness will be more persistent than previously forecast.	13	1
201512	933	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Developments on the second leg of our dual mandate have been significantly less encouraging.	13	1
201512	934	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Inflation has remained persistently below our 2 percent target for six years now despite substantial monetary accommodation.	13	1
201512	935	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Since the end of 2009, PCE inflation has averaged 1.4 percent, while core PCE inflation has averaged 1.5 percent.	13	1
201512	936	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Over this period, we have had 70 readings on the 12-month change in core PCE.	13	1
201512	937	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	In only four months has the rate been above 2 percent, and in these four months inflation was 2.1 percent or less.	13	1
201512	938	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	The recent price data give little hint that this undershooting of our target will end any time soon.	13	1
201512	939	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Although there may be reasons to expect inflation to rise gradually over the medium term, the forces that have kept it below our target have been remarkably persistent.	13	1
201512	940	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Indeed, on the basis of the descriptions of the alternative simulations in the Tealbook, it is noteworthy how hard you have to work to generate rates of inflation that exceed 2 percent in 2017 and 2018.	13	1
201512	941	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	The Phillips curve remains inert, a tiny fraction of its former self.	13	1
201512	942	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	There are also some hints that the persistent underperformance of inflation may be beginning to have some effect on inflation expectations, as some others have noted.	13	1
201512	943	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Although survey data had remained fairly steady, some recent readings have drifted lower.	13	1
201512	944	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Projections in the Survey of Professional Forecasters suggest that 10-year-ahead inflation expectations edged lower this quarter, although they have remained at or very near 2 percent since the end of 2012.	13	1
201512	945	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Over the past year, the median 5- to 10-year-ahead inflation expectation in the Michigan survey has averaged 2.7 percent, below the average reading over the past 10 years, and the preliminary December reading was 2.6 percent.	13	1
201512	946	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	This edging down in survey measures follows pronounced and persistent deterioration in market-based measures.	13	1
201512	947	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	The recent data on TIPS and nominal Treasury yields, as well as swaps, show that inflation compensation has remained near the very low levels reached at the beginning of this year.	13	1
201512	948	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Overall, these data, together with the persistent underperformance of actual inflation, raise some risk that inflation expectations could deteriorate.	13	1
201512	949	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	I would note in that regard that roughly half of the SEP submissions now assess risks to core inflation as tilted to the downside, and, of course, I am among that half.	13	1
201512	950	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Finally, although the risks from the domestic components of aggregate demand appear roughly balanced overall, I continue to be concerned about downside risk arising from the foreign outlook.	13	1
201512	951	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Although recent data suggest some improvement in foreign growth in the third quarter, growth is still very low, and risks remain, as evidenced by the recent volatility in commodities prices.	13	1
201512	952	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Growth in many advanced economies is quite feeble, despite unprecedented monetary accommodation.	13	1
201512	953	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	The recent data on Japan have improved, but third-quarter growth was still only 1 percent.	13	1
201512	954	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	In the euro area, GDP increased at an annual rate of only 1.2 percent last quarter, and challenges remain.	13	1
201512	955	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	In Japan, fiscal constraints threaten to derail growth in coming years, and slow growth, along with elevated fiscal debts, make many other advanced economies vulnerable to adverse shocks.	13	1
201512	956	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Oil prices, as has been noted, have resumed their downward slide, with a further decline of 19 percent over the intermeeting period.	13	1
201512	957	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	And although supply remains an important driver, the 10 percent further decline in metals prices suggests weak global demand is also at play.	13	1
201512	958	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	This adds further terms-of-trade pressures to the complicated policy challenges facing many emerging markets that are contending with a significant slowing in economic growth following a prolonged period with elevated growth in private-sector debt.	13	1
201512	959	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Emerging market growth slowed from an average of nearly 5 percent from 2010 to 2013 to a little over 3 percent last year and to 2¼ percent in the first half of this year.	13	1
201512	960	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	As you saw in the Tealbook, although growth has moved up somewhat last quarter to 3 percent, it still remains low.	13	1
201512	961	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	If economic growth remains low and exchange rate pressures rise, the ability to service some of the earlier accumulations in debt may be called into question and financial stresses may emerge.	13	1
201512	962	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	The transition to slower growth in China, in particular, remains an important risk to global economic and financial conditions.	13	1
201512	963	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	The recent data on economic activity have been mixed but overall suggest a continued gradual slowdown.	13	1
201512	964	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Recent weeks have seen evidence of increased foreign exchange intervention along with additional depreciation of the currency and a widening in the spread between the onshore and offshore currency markets.	13	1
201512	965	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Following the SDR announcement, the depreciation of the currency resumed at an accelerated pace, and we have seen a further 2 percent decline against the dollar in total during the intermeeting period.	13	1
201512	966	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Most recently, the PBOC’s suggestion of a shift to a weighted basket of currencies has raised some questions about possible further depreciation against the dollar.	13	1
201512	967	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	The continued unsettled nature of the Chinese exchange rate arrangements pose risk of further volatility.	13	1
201512	968	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	And, of course, with China accounting for over 20 percent in the trade-weighted dollar index, further downward movements in the renminbi against the dollar could have important knock-on effects.	13	1
201512	969	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	More broadly, the intermeeting period has seen a further 2 percent increase in the real dollar, bringing total strengthening up to about 16 percent since the summer of last year.	13	1
201512	970	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	As a result, the staff expects net exports to subtract a little over ½ percentage point from real GDP growth this year and 1 percentage point next year.	13	1
201512	971	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Further appreciation in response to weak foreign demand poses downside risks to this outlook and, conversely, dollar appreciation in response to stronger US growth may temper the impact of upside surprises here.	13	1
201512	972	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Finally, it is worth referencing the earlier presentation on the proximity of the zero lower bound, which accentuates the asymmetry in the risks to the outlook arising from adverse developments, whether foreign or domestic.	13	1
201512	973	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	As illustrated in the Tealbook, the federal funds rate has been cut by an average of 275 basis points over the five most moderate recessions since 1960.	13	1
201512	974	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	To the extent that the zero lower bound is a binding constraint, this implies a more severe recession in the event of an adverse shock.	13	1
201512	975	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	With the most recent Survey of Market Participants placing the probability of returning to the zero lower bound within the next two years at 25 percent, this is an important consideration.	13	1
201512	976	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	I may be more cautious than others around this table about the feasibility or advisability of viewing negative interest rates and QE as regular parts of our peacetime policy toolkit.	13	1
201512	977	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	I believe there are special costs and discontinuities associated with initiating such unconventional policies.	13	1
201512	978	2015-12-16	meeting	BRAINARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201512	979	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	13	1
201512	980	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Fischer.	13	1
201512	981	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201512	982	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Before I read the Tealbook last week, I had expected it to show an unchanged or weaker outlook than was presented in October.	13	1
201512	983	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	I had that impression, I suppose, mainly because the newspapers and outside forecasters and newsletters had seemed less than positive as of late, but I guess their job is to report the bad news more than the good news.	13	1
201512	984	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	So I was pleased and a bit surprised to see that, in fact, the staff’s interpretation of recent events has led to a modest strengthening of their outlook.	13	1
201512	985	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Further, as I read the Tealbook, I found their version of how economic events might unfold to be reasonably persuasive.	13	1
201512	986	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Real GDP growth seems likely to continue to rise a little faster than 2 percent in the next few years, aided next year by a pickup in federal spending, and the unemployment rate seems likely to fall further.	13	1
201512	987	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	At the same time, inflation seems likely to rise, albeit slowly.	13	1
201512	988	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	That conclusion depends in significant part on forecasts of the price of oil.	13	1
201512	989	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	In the past month or so, the price of oil has declined from levels of about $50 per barrel, a value at which many had begun to think it would stabilize, to under $40 per barrel.	13	1
201512	990	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	And with inventories high and OPEC no longer acting like a cartel, the price of oil may take longer to stabilize than had been anticipated until fairly recently.	13	1
201512	991	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	The other key factor in forecasts of both inflation and output is the exchange rate, and it remains to be seen to what extent foreign exchange markets have priced in the impact of a possible change in the federal funds rate, a topic we discussed earlier in the day with the staff.	13	1
201512	992	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Nonetheless, I believe that inflation is likely to follow approximately the path that the staff forecast and the SEP see for it.	13	1
201512	993	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	I’d like to mention three key elements in the staff forecast.	13	1
201512	994	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	They are, first, developments in the rest of the world; second, productivity growth; and third, r*.	13	1
201512	995	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	With regard to the first point, economic performance in the rest of the world, the staff’s analysis is slightly more optimistic than it was a few months ago, with China apparently on the road to a growth rate of 6½ percent or more, and with some positive signs coming out of the euro area, with the staff expecting growth to return to 2 percent–plus within a year from now.	13	1
201512	996	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	The ECB is clearly determined to run an accommodative monetary policy, which is far different than its behavior of a few years ago, and the euro-area economy is the second largest in the world.	13	1
201512	997	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Second, structural labor productivity growth over the period from 2011 to 2014 declined to an average annual rate of 0.8 percent, mainly as a result of a decline in multifactor productivity growth, which increased at a rate of only 0.1 percent per annum over that period.	13	1
201512	998	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	This year, the staff estimates that multifactor productivity growth will increase to just 0.3 percent, a rate that is expected to increase gradually to 0.7 percent by 2018.	13	1
201512	999	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	This projected increase in multifactor productivity accounts for the bulk of the increase in the staff forecast in structural labor productivity.	13	1
201512	1000	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	And that increase is critical in returning potential output growth to close to 2 percent, despite the staff’s and everyone else’s predictions of continuing declines in the labor force participation rate and a slower growth of labor supply.	13	1
201512	1001	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	A third issue is the increase in the staff’s estimate of the Tealbook-consistent FRB/US- based r* estimate.	13	1
201512	1002	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	As shown on page 2 of Tealbook B, this estimate rose from 0.74 percent in October to 1.24 percent this round.	13	1
201512	1003	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	This is a reflection of the staff’s view that some factors, mainly fiscal spending, have boosted the underlying strength of the economy enough that we don’t need monetary policy to be as expansionary to close the output gap as we did the previous time we estimated r*.	13	1
201512	1004	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	That seems like a remarkably large upward revision in a forecast round in which the staff describes the revisions as a “modest upgrade.”	13	1
201512	1005	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	When we discussed with the staff how this revision compares with those in the past, it turns out that revisions are often in the range of 25 basis points and that a 50 basis point move like this one is not that rare.	13	1
201512	1006	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	We had another one between July and September.	13	1
201512	1007	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Perhaps that underscores why using more than one measure of r* to gauge the stance of policy is good practice, and it also draws our attention to the fact that in the FRB/US model—and, I believe, in the real world—r* can be significantly affected by policies other than monetary policy.	13	1
201512	1008	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	The fact that the modest upward revision in fiscal spending leads to a positive growth outcome takes me to another important point.	13	1
201512	1009	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	We’re all typically reluctant to voice our views about the appropriate stance of fiscal policy because that isn’t our job and we shouldn’t presume to tell the Congress and the administration what to do.	13	1
201512	1010	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	But fiscal policy has a direct bearing on monetary policy.	13	1
201512	1011	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	If fiscal policy were substantially more supportive than it has been, we might have been able to get off the zero lower bound sooner and perhaps be further away from it when, inevitably, we are hit with another recessionary shock sometime in the future.	13	1
201512	1012	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	In addition, if the fiscal spending were put to good use, making investments in infrastructure and technology that will eventually boost productivity, that would also make the tradeoffs that the economy faces more appealing.	13	1
201512	1013	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	We don’t make fiscal policy, but fiscal policy can help significantly in producing growth, and we should consider how best to draw the attention of the policy community to this consequential point.	13	1
201512	1014	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	I’d also like, possibly for the second or third time, to discuss the frequent assertion that every central bank that raised its interest rate from the ZLB has had to return it to zero.	13	1
201512	1015	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Well, I’m one of those who raised the interest rate in 2009 and later reduced it.	13	1
201512	1016	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	There was nothing inevitable about the return to zero when it was raised.	13	1
201512	1017	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Israel began raising the interest rate in mid-2009, when the economy was growing well, and with inflation above the target range in large part because of increases in the price of housing.	13	1
201512	1018	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	That was the appropriate thing to do.	13	1
201512	1019	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Then came the euro crisis.	13	1
201512	1020	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	The Israeli economic situation deteriorated, and it became necessary to reduce the interest rate.	13	1
201512	1021	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	So it’s not clear to me what the message is of the much-quoted fact that countries that raise the interest rate from the lower bound later returned it to there.	13	1
201512	1022	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	By the same token, some years from now, we will be able to say that every country that reduced the interest rate to the zero lower bound later had to raise it from there.	13	1
201512	1023	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	[Laughter]	13	1
201512	1024	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	That would not mean that the rate should not have been reduced, but it might well mean that the emphasis on the rate having to be reduced by countries that had raised it is misplaced.	13	1
201512	1025	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	The simple question we need to answer today is whether we should raise the interest rate from its current level.	13	1
201512	1026	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	And I believe the considered answer to that question is “yes,” which we’ll talk about tomorrow.	13	1
201512	1027	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	My views do differ slightly from the Tealbook on the balance of risks.	13	1
201512	1028	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	On page 69 of Book A, the staff says that it says that it views the risk to the GDP outlook as “tilted somewhat to the downside.”	13	1
201512	1029	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	I believe that, if anything, the risks are slightly on the upside.	13	1
201512	1030	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Let me give a few factors.	13	1
201512	1031	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	First, by sending the message that the federal funds rate is not stuck at zero, we will be encouraging potential investors to invest now before interest rates rise again.	13	1
201512	1032	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	And, as I think I also mentioned before, this was the subject of Ben Bernanke’s Ph.D. thesis.	13	1
201512	1033	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	It was about waiting to invest, a topic that was very important around the beginning of the 1980s when he wrote his thesis and when the economy didn’t seem to be getting off the dime.	13	1
201512	1034	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Second, while we focus with concern on the negative effects of the latest decline in the price of oil on inflation, we should also consider its effects on demand.	13	1
201512	1035	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	The robust consumer spending in recent quarters, especially the strong auto sales in recent months, may well be strengthened by the continuing decline in energy prices.	13	1
201512	1036	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Third, if the modest upward movement we’ve seen in wage increases turns out to prove persistent as well, which is an upside risk, personal consumption expenditures in 2016 could turn out to be stronger than currently projected in the Tealbook.	13	1
201512	1037	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Fourth, over the longer term, it is quite possible that we will be surprised to the upside by productivity growth.	13	1
201512	1038	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	In a forum like this one, one thinks of Alan Greenspan in 1995 saying that he sensed that there was something going on with productivity, and one thinks also of Bob Solow saying that one sees computers everywhere except in the GDP data.	13	1
201512	1039	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	The revolutionary changes in the way we live and work using mobile technologies, including powerful search engines for everything and the ways businesses are learning to harness robotics and machine intelligence, will eventually find their way into the productivity statistics.	13	1
201512	1040	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	The delays may be long, but there is a decent upside risk that productivity growth will increase by more than we currently expect in the next few years.	13	1
201512	1041	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	I’ll say more on the consequences of all this in tomorrow’s remarks.	13	1
201512	1042	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
