201512	1400	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Vice Chairman.	13	1
201512	1401	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201512	1402	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	On balance, I think the economy’s forward momentum remains intact, but I think the risks to that growth momentum lie mainly on the downside.	13	1
201512	1403	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	While the effects of the inventory cycle will undoubtedly prove short-lived, the impact of the stronger dollar and slow foreign growth on US trade performance is likely to prove more persistent, as documented in the Tealbook.	13	1
201512	1404	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	The effects of this are already visible in US manufacturing by some measures.	13	1
201512	1405	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	I did take some signal from the most recent ISM manufacturing index, which dipped below 50 percent last month.	13	1
201512	1406	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	That’s the first time it’s been below that mark in three years.	13	1
201512	1407	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	My concern is this:  The persistent trade drag will slow the economy, and this in turn will lead to slower payroll employment growth.	13	1
201512	1408	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	If that were to happen, that would cut into household income growth, and that could take some of the steam out of consumer spending.	13	1
201512	1409	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	Now, we’re clearly not seeing that yet—employment gains remain healthy, and the most recent retail sales report was solid—but I do think this is a real risk to the outlook.	13	1
201512	1410	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	I think the risks to the outlook are mainly about what’s happening abroad.	13	1
201512	1411	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	I think those risks are still very much present.	13	1
201512	1412	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	The OPEC decision to increase their production quota at a time when oil prices are weak and inventories are abundant has provoked another downward movement in oil prices, and this could intensify even further from here if inventories continue to accumulate and exhaust the available storage space.	13	1
201512	1413	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	In any case, I think we’re going to see a lot more stress on energy producers and major energy-exporting countries in 2016.	13	1
201512	1414	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	The fact is, existing price hedges are running off, and the new hedges, if they are put in place, will be set at much lower levels than a year ago.	13	1
201512	1415	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	For example, the WTI crude oil forward prices 12 months ahead are roughly $20 a barrel lower now than they were a year ago, so the December 2016 contract is trading at around $44 a barrel.	13	1
201512	1416	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	You don’t get that much if you sell oil forward anymore.	13	1
201512	1417	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	The stress, I think, on some emerging market economies also has increased further as a number of other commodity prices have hit new lows.	13	1
201512	1418	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	Also, it’s noteworthy that it’s not like the supply is not still coming out of Spain—there are a number of large-scale mining production facilities that are going to enter the market in 2016.	13	1
201512	1419	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	I think this is going to exacerbate the glut in commodities such as iron ore and copper.	13	1
201512	1420	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	In my mind, not only is there a risk of still lower prices, but this stress from lower prices is likely to prove persistent for quite some time.	13	1
201512	1421	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	I focus on both the degree of stress and the persistence of stress because I think that the more severe the stress is and the longer it lasts, the greater the chance of breakage.	13	1
201512	1422	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	That breakage could include large corporate failures, big capital flow reversals, or pronounced currency weakness.	13	1
201512	1423	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	If that were to occur, the degree of stress could increase even further.	13	1
201512	1424	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	For example, currency weakness could exacerbate the burden of dollar-denominated debt, and that would increase the risk of additional breakage.	13	1
201512	1425	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	The result could be a self-reinforcing dynamic that could lead to a much worse outcome than what we currently anticipate.	13	1
201512	1426	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	I see the financial crisis and the Great Recession as one example of this dynamic at work.	13	1
201512	1427	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	In the fall of 2007, we did not appreciate what was going to come our way over the next few years.	13	1
201512	1428	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	As the stress intensified and persisted, more and more things broke, and I think this just shows the limits of model-based forecasts that have trouble incorporating these types of reinforcing dynamics.	13	1
201512	1429	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	With respect to China, the good news is that the transition to more-balanced growth is under way, but I do think people may be a bit too optimistic about the ability of the Chinese to manage this process and the risks that have already been created by the sharp rise in indebtedness that’s occurred there among major corporates and local government entities.	13	1
201512	1430	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	The prevailing view about China seems to be that while there eventually could be a hard landing—the fact is the buildup of debt there is very striking—it’s not going to happen yet.	13	1
201512	1431	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	That’s because the government still has plenty of policy instruments that it can use to cushion the adjustment and a view that the policymakers are highly competent.	13	1
201512	1432	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	Now, that’s probably the right view.	13	1
201512	1433	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	What happens if it turns out that the hard landing happens much sooner than what we currently anticipate?	13	1
201512	1434	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	On the inflation side of the ledger, I continue to be less worried than some of us about core inflation being considerably below 2 percent.	13	1
201512	1435	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	There are several reasons for this.	13	1
201512	1436	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	First, I take some signal from the fact that the trend has been sideways rather than down given the fact that we’ve had energy prices and non-energy import prices pushing downward, so core inflation has been flat even though we’ve had these downward forces.	13	1
201512	1437	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	It seems to me that when those downward forces dissipate, core inflation should move back up.	13	1
201512	1438	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	Second, I do take some signal from the fact that the gap between core services inflation and core goods inflation is unusually wide right now, so that reinforces that first point.	13	1
201512	1439	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	This suggests to me that inflation will likely rise as that gap is closed by core goods inflation moving higher as the effects of the stronger dollar ultimately dissipate.	13	1
201512	1440	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	Third, I think wage trends are consistent with an economy that’s approaching full employment.	13	1
201512	1441	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	While it’s true that wage compensation trends, broadly defined, have not moved up much, I do take some signal from what we’ve seen because it does seem consistent with anecdotal reports in which businesses are telling us that it’s harder and harder to find people for certain types of positions—“truck driver” seems to be the one that I hear the most about.	13	1
201512	1442	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	Also, there may be offsetting factors holding down wage trends, such as the weak headline inflation trend and the fact that the underlying productivity growth trend seems to have fallen.	13	1
201512	1443	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	So the fact that some things that might be pushing nominal wage growth down and the fact that the wage compensation trend is broadly stable might be consistent with an economy that is, in fact, approaching full employment.	13	1
201512	1444	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	In contrast to the fact that the core inflation rate is a bit below 2 percent, which I’m not that anxious about, I do have some concerns about inflation expectations.	13	1
201512	1445	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	Some of the survey- based measures of inflation expectations show a slight downward trend, and although the University of Michigan measure over the next five years ticked back up to 2.6 percent in November, it remains at the very low end of the range of recent years.	13	1
201512	1446	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	Most notable to me is the decline in the Federal Reserve Bank of New York’s Survey of Consumer Expectations.	13	1
201512	1447	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	This is a three-year measure of inflation expectations.	13	1
201512	1448	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	So what happens?	13	1
201512	1449	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	For each individual, we calculate the mean, the median, and the 25th and 75th percentile of their three-year inflation density forecast, and all of these measures have dipped notably over the past year.	13	1
201512	1450	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	From January, they’ve declined between 30 to 50 basis points— that’s the mean, the median, and the 25th and 75th percentile.	13	1
201512	1451	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	What that’s telling you is that the whole distribution of inflation expectations for these individuals has shifted to the left.	13	1
201512	1452	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	And it seems hard to attribute this shift just to the drop in energy prices because, one, energy prices were dropping pretty sharply last January, and, two, unlike the University of Michigan five-by- five inflation expectations measure, the Federal Reserve Bank of New York three-year measure doesn’t seem to be nearly as sensitive to the changes in oil and gas prices.	13	1
201512	1453	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	I want to point you to the Federal Reserve Bank of New York’s Survey of Consumer Expectations because I think this survey actually has a much sturdier methodology for tracking inflation expectations compared with the University of Michigan measure.	13	1
201512	1454	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	The University of Michigan survey has been around a lot longer, I know, and that’s why we always cite it, but I think the Federal Reserve Bank of New York survey is actually a better survey.	13	1
201512	1455	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	The sample size is much bigger, and it’s conducted so that most of the respondents are the same month to month, so you’re following the same people over time, which eliminates a lot of the sampling volatility in the results.	13	1
201512	1456	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	And the question about inflation expectations is better crafted to elicit well- informed responses about inflation expectations.	13	1
201512	1457	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	We ask about inflation—the University of Michigan survey asks about prices.	13	1
201512	1458	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	Now, of course, the survey has a much shorter track record—it only goes back a couple of years.	13	1
201512	1459	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	But if it’s changes in inflation expectations from survey measures that we care about, then there’s a good case to put considerable weight on the New York survey results and not just always cite the University of Michigan measures.	13	1
201512	1460	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	When I put all of this together—no significant change in the growth outlook, considerable risk from abroad, and inflation expectations in some danger of becoming unhinged to the downside—that suggests to me that there’s not a slam-dunk case for tightening at this meeting or, for that matter, concluding that not tightening in September was a mistake.	13	1
201512	1461	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	At the same time, these risks may not materialize, so I think it’s inappropriate to wait any longer.	13	1
201512	1462	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	There are always risks, and with the unemployment rate now close to most of our estimates of the longer-run unemployment rate, I don’t think we should wait any longer, as long as we believe the economy is likely to continue to grow at an above-trend pace, even if only slightly.	13	1
201512	1463	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	So I think the current situation calls for a go-slow strategy until we see either the economy’s forward momentum is sustained or the inflation outlook evolves in a manner consistent with even greater confidence that inflation will head back to 2 percent over the medium term or both.	13	1
201512	1464	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	That’s what I’ve signaled with the my SEP submission—only two 25 basis point tightenings in 2016, and then, as we get more confident, a faster pace thereafter.	13	1
201512	1465	2015-12-16	meeting	DUDLEY	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201512	1466	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	13	1
201512	1467	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	And thank you to everyone for a very thoughtful round of comments on the economic outlook and the risks.	13	1
201512	1468	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	I would just like to wrap up with a few comments of my own, including some observations on the policy implications of the outlook and the uncertainties we face in anticipating tomorrow’s discussion.	13	1
201512	1469	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Let me start with the labor market.	13	1
201512	1470	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Back in October, I was concerned that the soft tone of the data we had received coming into that meeting might be a sign that a persistent broad-based slowing in the pace of labor market improvement was under way.	13	1
201512	1471	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Fortunately, that risk now seems far less likely, in light of the past two monthly reports, which I think everyone would agree were quite favorable.	13	1
201512	1472	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Payrolls grew about 220,000 per month, on average, from September through November, and that’s about the same solid pace we observed over the past 12 months.	13	1
201512	1473	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	The unemployment rate has continued to edge down in recent months, and, at 5 percent, it’s 0.7 percentage point lower than last January and only a shade above the median of our projections of its longer-run sustainable level.	13	1
201512	1474	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Broader measures of labor utilization have also improved substantially.	13	1
201512	1475	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	The U-6 rate, for example, has fallen almost 1½ percentage points since the start of the year.	13	1
201512	1476	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Labor force participation has declined since the start of the year, and the employment-to-population ratio is unchanged.	13	1
201512	1477	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	But these developments, nonetheless, represent a cyclical improvement in labor market conditions, in light of ongoing demographically driven declines in their underlying trends.	13	1
201512	1478	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	So, to my mind, overall, the data confirm that underutilization of labor resources has diminished appreciably over the past year.	13	1
201512	1479	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	That said, I continue to think, as a number of you do, that the economy is not quite back to full employment.	13	1
201512	1480	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	The unemployment rate is still ¼ percentage point above my own estimate of its longer-run level.	13	1
201512	1481	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	The share of employees working part time for economic reasons remains about 1 percentage point above its pre-recession level, and I’m more optimistic than the staff that a healthy job market will pull people back into the labor market.	13	1
201512	1482	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	In addition, wage growth, as measured by the ECI and average hourly earnings on a year-over-year basis, remains soft, suggesting not only that the labor market is not all that tight, but that our estimates of the natural rate of unemployment might be too high.	13	1
201512	1483	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	That said, a number of you mentioned indications of rising wage pressures from your contacts, and it’s a theme I’ve also heard in many recent meetings with business leaders.	13	1
201512	1484	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	In addition, the recent marked acceleration in compensation per hour on a year-over-year basis, coupled with monthly gains in average hourly earnings this fall that have been somewhat greater on average than those seen earlier in the year, could be signaling the start of a sustained pickup in wages after years of stagnation.	13	1
201512	1485	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	And, of course, I would also see that as a welcome development in line with the Tealbook forecast, but I agree with those of you who have pointed out that wage measures, especially compensation per hour, are very noisy indicators, and we should keep in mind that earlier this year we thought we were seeing signs of a pickup in wages, and it subsequently faded.	13	1
201512	1486	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	With regard to spending and production indicators, on balance, the incoming data point to continued moderate growth in real activity.	13	1
201512	1487	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Motor vehicle sales have been robust, retail sales are advancing at a solid pace, and consumer confidence has moved up recently and currently stands at a relatively high level.	13	1
201512	1488	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Housing continues its gradual recovery, and business fixed investment appears to be expanding steadily outside the drilling and mining sector.	13	1
201512	1489	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Even there, reduced drilling should restrain overall GDP growth much less in the coming year as the contraction bottoms out and the sector shrinks.	13	1
201512	1490	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Of course, the relative strength of domestic spending is being partially offset by weakness in net exports, and that is a drag that is likely to persist for some time, due to the appreciation of the dollar and the current weakness in foreign growth.	13	1
201512	1491	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	But the potential risks to the US economy from global financial and economic developments, although still quite material, at least in my view, have diminished since late summer.	13	1
201512	1492	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Overall, I expect that real GDP growth will continue to run a bit ahead of potential output growth, thereby generating further improvements in labor market conditions in coming months.	13	1
201512	1493	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	On the inflation front, during the intermeeting period, the data have been largely in line with expectations.	13	1
201512	1494	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	My outlook is little changed.	13	1
201512	1495	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	For this year, overall PCE inflation appears poised to come in a bit below ½ percent, a shade lower than the staff projected in October.	13	1
201512	1496	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	But barring some major surprise, by the March meeting, headline inflation will probably have jumped to around 1 percent on a 12-month basis, as the big declines in energy prices recorded a year ago drop out of the index.	13	1
201512	1497	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Core inflation at that point is likely to be close to 1½ percent, a touch higher than currently.	13	1
201512	1498	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Thereafter, although the lingering effects of recent movements in oil prices and the dollar may keep inflation subdued for much of the rest of 2016, I am at least reasonably confident that once these transitory influences finally dissipate, inflation over the next two or three years will return to 2 percent, aided by a further tightening in resource utilization.	13	1
201512	1499	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	So what does all of this imply for monetary policy?	13	1
201512	1500	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	With regard to the decision at this meeting, my own judgment is that current economic conditions and the outlook, taken together, now warrant a modest increase in the target range for the federal funds rate.	13	1
201512	1501	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Three considerations lead me to this conclusion.	13	1
201512	1502	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	First, as I just noted, we have seen further improvement in the labor market, and I’m reasonably confident that inflation will rise to 2 percent over the medium term.	13	1
201512	1503	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Thus, the two conditions for liftoff that we announced back in March have now been met to my satisfaction.	13	1
201512	1504	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Second, monetary policy operates with a substantial lag, and waiting to act until we’re closer to achieving our dual objectives risks disrupting the economy in the future because we might be forced to tighten abruptly.	13	1
201512	1505	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	And, finally, and very importantly, monetary policy will remain appropriately accommodative if we do decide to raise the target range by 25 basis points.	13	1
201512	1506	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	This assessment primarily follows from my judgment that a further fall in the unemployment rate would be desirable both to help take up the labor market slack that remains and to speed the return to 2 percent inflation.	13	1
201512	1507	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	A simple back-of-the-envelope calculation suggests that the effective stance of policy after liftoff should help to produce these conditions without being overly stimulative.	13	1
201512	1508	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Let’s assume that the equilibrium real federal funds rate is currently about zero, consistent with the analysis presented at the October meeting.	13	1
201512	1509	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Increasing the target range by 25 basis points would, therefore, leave the real federal funds rate roughly 100 basis points below the equilibrium rate, as core inflation is currently running a little below 1½ percent.	13	1
201512	1510	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Simulations of the FRB/US model and the Laubach-Williams model suggest that keeping the gap between the real federal funds rate and the equilibrium rate constant at this level for a couple of years would be expected to push the unemployment rate only ¼ to ½ percentage point or so below its longer-run sustainable level, all else being equal, providing a modest boost to inflation.	13	1
201512	1511	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	This simple calculation suggests to me that we needn’t be in a hurry to close the real federal funds rate gap, as the risk of excessively overheating the economy seems low.	13	1
201512	1512	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	That said, our economic projections imply that the federal funds rate will likely have to rise gradually over the next few years even if we were to decide that it is appropriate to keep the gap between the real federal funds rate and the equilibrium rate constant.	13	1
201512	1513	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	As trend inflation gradually converges back to 2 percent, the nominal federal funds rate will need to move up more or less in tandem to avoid an inadvertent easing in the effective stance of policy.	13	1
201512	1514	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Similarly, the federal funds rate, both real and nominal, will need to rise over the next few years as the headwinds still restraining real activity fade—that is, if r* rises gradually as we expect.	13	1
201512	1515	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Of course, real activity and inflation could evolve in materially different ways from what we now expect, and so we should be wary of being too confident about the appropriate future path of policy.	13	1
201512	1516	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Furthermore, taking a cautious approach to tightening remains appropriate in light of the asymmetric risk posed by the effective lower bound in the present circumstances.	13	1
201512	1517	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	And, finally, we should proceed cautiously in light of heightened uncertainty about the economic effects of higher interest rates.	13	1
201512	1518	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	In part, this increased uncertainty reflects the fact that our monetary policy is now atypically diverging from that of the rest of the world, and, as a result, we may see unusually large exchange rate effects.	13	1
201512	1519	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Other sources of increased uncertainty are the changes that have occurred over the past eight years in credit availability, capital standards, and other aspects of the financial system, which may have reduced the sensitivity of aggregate activity to interest rates.	13	1
201512	1520	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	And the taper tantrum episode reminds us that the response of financial markets to a change in policy can be hard to predict.	13	1
201512	1521	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Although these considerations argue in favor of proceeding cautiously in adjusting the stance of monetary policy, especially in the early going, they do not imply that we should stand pat for as long as inflation remains subdued.	13	1
201512	1522	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	For example, if the labor market were to continue to improve markedly as we move through 2016, then further moderate increases in the federal funds rate would probably be warranted, even if core inflation was still showing no signs of picking up.	13	1
201512	1523	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Although we might consider lowering our estimates of the natural rate of unemployment a bit in response to such developments, it would also be prudent to view them as a sign that the underlying strength of the economy was in fact increasing, and that inflation would move up as labor and product markets tighten.	13	1
201512	1524	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Accordingly, we would want to check the pace of employment growth somewhat to reduce the risk of overheating that could eventually force us to tighten abruptly, with potentially adverse effects on the economy.	13	1
201512	1525	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Of course, if inflation were to remain persistently subdued beyond next year despite further improvements in the labor market and no special transitory factors were in play, then, in my view, a more radical rethinking of the economy’s productive potential would surely be in order.	13	1
201512	1526	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	So, let me stop there with those comments.	13	1
201512	1527	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	I think we have time to turn to Thomas for his briefing on monetary policy alternatives before we break for dinner.	21	2
201512	1528	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	Thank you, Madam Chair.	21	2

201512	1530	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	One key issue for tomorrow is whether to raise the target range for the federal funds rate.	21	2
201512	1531	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	Just as important, as you emphasized in your discussion at the October meeting, is that tomorrow’s statement effectively communicate the Committee’s current thinking about the likely future path of the federal funds rate as well as the economic conditionality of the expected policy rate path.	21	2
201512	1532	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	The three draft statements in the handout provide options for addressing these two issues.	21	2
201512	1533	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	Alternatives A, B, and C offer somewhat different combinations of assessments of current and expected economic developments bearing on the Committee’s decision on the policy rate.	21	2
201512	1534	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	As indicated in the box at the top of your first exhibit, all three alternatives report further improvement in a range of labor market indicators over the intermeeting period and say that those developments confirm an appreciable improvement in underutilization of labor resources since early this year.	21	2
201512	1535	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	On inflation, both alternatives B and C characterize inflation as continuing to run below the Committee’s objective in part because of declines in energy prices and prices of non- energy imports.	21	2
201512	1536	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	However, they offer somewhat different perspectives on recent movements in measures of inflation expectations.	21	2
201512	1537	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	Alternative B highlights the fact that market-based measures are low and that survey-based measures have “edged down,” while alternative C characterizes those measures, respectively, as having “stabilized” and having “generally remained stable.”	21	2
201512	1538	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	In describing the outlook for inflation in paragraph 2, both alternatives B and C reaffirm the expectation that inflation will rise to 2 percent over the medium term as the transitory factors currently holding down inflation dissipate and the labor market strengthens further.	21	2
201512	1539	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	And, in announcing the policy action in paragraph 3, both alternatives express reasonable confidence in that forecast.	21	2
201512	1540	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	However, alternative B includes a couple of indications that the Committee is viewing the outlook for inflation cautiously.	21	2
201512	1541	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	Alternative B retains the final sentence of paragraph 2 in the October statement, which says “the Committee continues to monitor inflation developments closely.”	21	2
201512	1542	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	And paragraph 4 emphasizes the Committee’s intention to carefully monitor actual and expected progress toward its inflation goal.	21	2
201512	1543	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	Alternative A says that the Committee is not sufficiently confident in the outlook for inflation to warrant a change in the target range for the federal funds rate.	21	2
201512	1544	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	In explaining the decision to leave the funds rate unchanged, the Committee would cite “subdued” inflation, core inflation, and gains in labor compensation and “low” measures of inflation expectations.	21	2
201512	1545	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	Paragraph 1 reports that the current shortfall of inflation from 2 percent is “only partly” attributable to transitory factors.	21	2
201512	1546	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	Paragraph 2 suggests a risk that too-low inflation might persist by saying that the temporary factors holding down inflation will “eventually” dissipate; paragraph 2 also reports that the Committee sees a need to “closely monitor” measures of both actual and expected inflation.	21	2
201512	1547	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	If it were to adopt alternative A, the Committee would drop the criteria for liftoff that it first communicated in March.	21	2
201512	1548	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	Instead,  it would say that how long to maintain the current federal funds rate target would depend on “realized and expected” progress toward its maximum employment and inflation objectives, and it would add that it is prepared to provide additional accommodation if incoming information does not soon indicate that inflation is moving up toward 2 percent.	21	2
201512	1549	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	The box at the bottom of exhibit 1 summarizes how alternatives B and C communicate the Committee’s thinking about the expected policy rate path as you go forward.	21	2
201512	1550	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	Paragraph 2 of alternative B indicates that the Committee’s economic outlook is consistent with “gradual” adjustments in the stance of policy.	21	2
201512	1551	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	Then, in paragraph 4, alternative B describes the Committee’s expectation that “economic conditions will evolve in a manner that will warrant only gradual increases in the federal funds rate.”	21	2
201512	1552	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	By contrast, alternative C refers to “appropriate” rather than “gradual” policy adjustments in paragraph 2 and omits the “only” in paragraph 4.	21	2
201512	1553	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	Both alternatives state the Committee’s expectation that “the funds rate is likely to remain, for some time, below levels that are expected to prevail in the longer run.”	21	2
201512	1554	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	Both alternatives underline economic conditionality by saying, in paragraph 4, that “the timing and size of future adjustments to the target range” will depend on “realized and expected economic conditions relative to [the Committee’s] objectives” and then adding that “the actual path of the federal funds rate will depend on the economic outlook as informed by incoming data.”	21	2
201512	1555	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	The next exhibit examines how your policy strategy is currently understood by financial markets.	21	2
201512	1556	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	Recall that in March 2014, you first introduced statement language indicating that “economic conditions may, for some time, warrant keeping the target federal funds rate below levels” viewed “as normal in the longer run.”	21	2
201512	1557	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	This message has been reinforced over the past year by your SEP submissions as well as other communications.	21	2
201512	1558	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	The median of primary dealers’ modal expectations for the path of the federal funds rate, shown by the blue dots in the upper-left panel of exhibit 2, is very close to the median of your most recent policy projections, the green diamonds.	21	2
201512	1559	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	In contrast, the policy rate path derived from OIS quotes continues to run well below the median of modal expectations in the primary dealer survey.	21	2
201512	1560	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	Based on these quotes, the federal funds rate is expected to increase only about 50 basis points over the first year following the onset of tightening.	21	2
201512	1561	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	But, as discussed in a box in Tealbook B, this gap does not necessarily imply that the modal outlook for the federal funds rate embedded in these quotes is much different from that of the dealer survey or the SEP.	21	2
201512	1562	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	As shown in the upper-right panel, market quotes point to an expected pace of tightening that is substantially slower than it was at the onset of tightening in early 1994, the blue line, and mid-2004, the red line.	21	2
201512	1563	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	Whether this observation indicates a correct understanding by market participants of your intended strategy depends on the economic conditions on which this expectation is predicated.	21	2
201512	1564	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	While we do not observe the expectations for economic outcomes on which these market quotes are based, the middle two panels, taken from the Survey of Professional Forecasters, suggest that these forecasters assign the highest probability to outcomes similar to those in your SEP.	21	2
201512	1565	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	I was advised that these panels are a little adventuresome, so let me just quickly say that I will certainly check afterward with President Evans on the effects that these panels have on the viewer.	21	2
201512	1566	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	Each column here essentially represents an SPF vintage, with the most recent one being the right-most column, and the height of the bars of different colors in each of these columns represents the probability mass placed on the outcomes being shown underneath.	21	2
201512	1567	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	In particular, the dark blue portion at the right edge of the middle-left panel shows that forecasters currently see GDP growth over the year ahead in the 2 to 3 percent range as the most likely outcome, while the light blue portion at the right edge of the middle-right panel shows that they similarly place highest odds on PCE inflation next year falling in the 1 to 2 percent range.	21	2
201512	1568	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	It therefore seems plausible that if the economy evolves in a manner consistent with the median SEP outlook, market participants would be unlikely to alter their expectation of a tightening pace of 50 to 100 basis points per year.	21	2
201512	1569	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	By contrast, how market expectations regarding the path of the policy rate would adjust if the economy were to surprise is less clear.	21	2
201512	1570	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	Particularly striking is how little weight markets seem to place on the federal funds rate rising more than 150 basis points next year.	21	2
201512	1571	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	The lower-left panel shows the probability distribution for three-month LIBOR at the end of 2016 implied by options on Eurodollar futures.	21	2
201512	1572	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	The implied probability that the pace of tightening will exceed 150 basis points is merely 20 percent.	21	2
201512	1573	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	Similarly, the odds that the SPF respondents place on real GDP growing faster than 3 percent or inflation exceeding 2 percent are also about 20 percent each.	21	2
201512	1574	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	A more robust economic performance could cause a sharp market response as in 1994, when the expected pace of tightening—the blue line in the upper-right panel—and longer-term rates shot up over the course of the year.	21	2
201512	1575	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	While surprisingly rapid progress toward the Committee’s objectives could pose challenges for your communications by raising the question to what extent you would still view gradual adjustments to the federal funds rate as being appropriate, arguably the opposite risk—a lack of progress toward your objectives—would present even greater challenges.	21	2
201512	1576	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	One possible scenario on investors’ minds might be that inflation fails to rise as you project—a scenario that might be reflected in continued low readings of breakeven inflation.	21	2
201512	1577	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	As you know, decomposing breakeven inflation into expectations and risk premium components is challenging, and any such decomposition is model specific.	21	2
201512	1578	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	The black line in the lower-right panel shows the inflation expectations component derived from the standard specification of the staff’s four-factor model including nominal and TIPS yields.	21	2
201512	1579	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	That measure suggests that inflation expectations of these investors at the 5-to-10-year horizon have declined only marginally since the middle of last year.	21	2
201512	1580	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	However, this result is based on the maintained assumption that inflation will return, eventually, to the 1991–2014 sample average.	21	2
201512	1581	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	The red line shows that if this assumption is replaced by an assumption that inflation is nonstationary—that it need not revert to the sample average in the long run—the decline in inflation expectations since mid-2014 is estimated to have been substantially larger.	21	2
201512	1582	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	In the face of substantial uncertainty about the strength of forces moving inflation back to your objective, you may view the emphasis that alternative B places on a gradual approach to removing accommodation combined with a great deal of attention to inflation developments as a prudent approach to managing this risk.	21	2
201512	1583	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	Finally, as a housekeeping item, I should mention that, since circulating Tealbook B, we made two minor adjustments to the language of the directive to the Desk, which is shown in bold blue on page 12 in your handout.	21	2
201512	1584	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	The purpose of the second of these changes was to bring the language of the directive in line with the more accurate language that has been used for several years now in your postmeeting statements.	21	2
201512	1585	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	So you will find that, actually, the postmeeting statement has always been talking about “at auction.”	21	2
201512	1586	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	I should also mention that we are considering one other small change that I should bring to your attention.	21	2
201512	1587	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	On page 13, the language there refers to the “primary credit rate,” and we wanted to add that this refers to the discount rate—and put the primary credit rate in parentheses—because prior to 2008, statements referred to “the discount rate,” and we wanted to make sure that there is no confusion that “primary credit rate” might refer to something like “prime rate.”	21	2
201512	1588	2015-12-16	meeting	LAUBACH	Thank you, Madam Chair, I would be happy to take questions.	21	2

201512	1627	2015-12-16	meeting	WILLIAMS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201512	1628	2015-12-16	meeting	WILLIAMS	I unequivocally support alternative B as written.	23	2
201512	1629	2015-12-16	meeting	WILLIAMS	The data convincingly support this decision, according to the conditions that we laid out.	23	2
201512	1630	2015-12-16	meeting	WILLIAMS	Job growth has come in stronger than expected, and broad measures of labor underutilization have continued to improve.	23	2
201512	1631	2015-12-16	meeting	WILLIAMS	It appears likely that the economy will exceed full employment next year by even more than I had anticipated just a few months ago.	23	2
201512	1632	2015-12-16	meeting	WILLIAMS	Incoming price inflation data remain low, but this weakness largely reflects dollar appreciation and declines in energy and commodity prices.	23	2
201512	1633	2015-12-16	meeting	WILLIAMS	These transitory factors should dissipate as labor markets really start to be stretched next year, and I’m confident that inflation will move back to our 2 percent target over the next couple of years.	23	2
201512	1634	2015-12-16	meeting	WILLIAMS	The downside risks to the outlook have also fallen substantially.	23	2
201512	1635	2015-12-16	meeting	WILLIAMS	Fears of a sharp slowdown in China have diminished, and a federal fiscal battle appears to have been avoided.	23	2
201512	1636	2015-12-16	meeting	WILLIAMS	The resilience of the economy over the past few months in the face of those headwinds has also been encouraging.	23	2
201512	1637	2015-12-16	meeting	WILLIAMS	Of course, the flip side of starting normalization now is, we can signal that the appropriate path will also be quite gradual, and the language in the statement does just that.	23	2
201512	1638	2015-12-16	meeting	WILLIAMS	Slow and steady increases in the funds rate should provide an appropriate tightening of broader financial conditions to maintain moderate growth and full employment in the face of continuing headwinds.	23	2
201512	1639	2015-12-16	meeting	WILLIAMS	I also support the language in paragraph 5 that signals that the reinvestment will continue until the funds rate normalization is well under way.	23	2
201512	1640	2015-12-16	meeting	WILLIAMS	This approach is supported by both communications and risk-management considerations.	23	2
201512	1641	2015-12-16	meeting	WILLIAMS	For the next year or so, it’s desirable to keep policy focused on our traditional tool of monetary policy, the short-term interest rate.	23	2
201512	1642	2015-12-16	meeting	WILLIAMS	Such a focus will concentrate the public’s attention on our policy message; center policy rate expectations; and, I hope, minimize confusion.	23	2
201512	1643	2015-12-16	meeting	WILLIAMS	Thank you.	23	2

201512	1645	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	President Evans.	23	2
201512	1646	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201512	1647	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	I can support alternative B today, in large part because of its important state-dependent characterization of our gradual adjustment path.	23	2
201512	1648	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	I find today to be a tough call.	23	2
201512	1649	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	I think the risk-management case for delay until mid-2016 remains strong.	23	2
201512	1650	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	Core PCE inflation continues to run well below our 2 percent objective.	23	2
201512	1651	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	Some of our best medium-term r* measures are at zero or below, and the statistical models suggest they could be very low for a long time.	23	2
201512	1652	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	In a global environment full of low-inflation risks, I think uncertainty arguments weigh strongly for further delay while we monitor inflation for signs of revival toward 2 percent.	23	2
201512	1653	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	After all, we know how to raise rates if inflation heads too high, but we don’t like our toolbox nearly as much if we face renewed disinflationary pressures.	23	2
201512	1654	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	But the big weakness in the argument for alternative A today is that most of our recent monetary policy communications by this Committee have signaled that data conditions and our outlook have met the threshold for liftoff.	23	2
201512	1655	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	Acting today seems appropriate to me as long as our first move is accompanied by a communication strategy that indicates that our initial adjustments will be gradual.	23	2
201512	1656	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	This strategy also needs to be clear that the path is state dependent, based on further confirmation that we are on track to achieve our dual-mandate goals over the medium term.	23	2
201512	1657	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	I believe that alternative B as written provides this clarity and strikes a reasonable balance among competing concerns.	23	2
201512	1658	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	Another important feature in alternative B is the language in paragraph 4 stating that the shortfall of inflation from 2 percent means the Committee needs to give special consideration to actual and expected progress toward our inflation target.	23	2
201512	1659	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	This language recognizes reality.	23	2
201512	1660	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	It acknowledges that the main challenge we face today is getting inflation back up to target.	23	2
201512	1661	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	It appropriately emphasizes our concern over this policy shortfall, and it seems about as close as we can get today to saying that we are committed to a symmetric inflation target.	23	2
201512	1662	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	As I’ve discussed here many times before, if we act as if our target is actually a ceiling, it will be all that much harder for us to ever achieve our policy mandate.	23	2
201512	1663	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	Most of us have said that we think we have a symmetric inflation target.	23	2
201512	1664	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	Let’s make sure we also act as if we do.	23	2
201512	1665	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	And I hope that we will talk more about symmetry in January during the annual review of our longer- run goals and policy strategy.	23	2
201512	1666	2015-12-16	meeting	EVANS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2

201512	1668	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	President Rosengren.	23	2

201512	1670	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	I support alternative B as written.	23	2

201512	1672	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	Labor markets have certainly improved, and it was good news that the past two employment reports have been so positive.	23	2
201512	1673	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	I am reasonably confident that inflation will reach 2 percent, at least in part based on the current tightness in the labor market.	23	2
201512	1674	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	However, as I highlighted yesterday, the biggest risk to my forecast is that inflation does not rise to 2 percent as anticipated, similar to the comments that President Evans just made.	23	2
201512	1675	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	As we raise rates, I would suggest that we continue along that path only as our confidence that our inflation target will be met improves from reasonable to high.	23	2
201512	1676	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	Since I expect the tangible evidence of movement toward our inflation target to be slow, I am quite comfortable with a normalization path that incorporates only a gradual increase in rates.	23	2
201512	1677	2015-12-16	meeting	ROSENGREN	If we don’t move from reasonable confidence to high confidence, I could easily imagine a pace of normalization slower than in my SEP.	23	2

201512	1681	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Fischer.	23	2
201512	1682	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201512	1683	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	I’m afraid I’m going to make a longer statement, but with the same result.	23	2
201512	1684	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	I favor raising the target federal funds rate to a range of 25 to 50 basis points.	23	2
201512	1685	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Because the FOMC has not raised the federal funds rate for nearly 10 years, because the rate was at its effective lower bound for more than 7 years, and because it was reduced to its present level at the height of the worst US financial crisis of the past 80 years, this move has acquired a significance that goes beyond the impact that would be expected on the basis of a 25 basis point increase in the federal funds rate in more normal circumstances.	23	2
201512	1686	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	The decision is significant also because it is the beginning of the process of normalization of monetary policy.	23	2
201512	1687	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	As the Chair and other members of this Committee have emphasized, most members of the FOMC expect that the normalization process will be gradual.	23	2
201512	1688	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	But we are all quick to add that the process will be data and outcome dependent, and that if prices and employment increase more rapidly than we currently anticipate, the future path of the interest rate will be steeper than we now anticipate.	23	2
201512	1689	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	We should and do emphasize, no less, that if the economy falters and prices and employment increase more slowly than we currently anticipate, the future path of the interest rate will be shallower than we now anticipate, and shallowness includes the possibility that the interest rate path may reverse its slope.	23	2
201512	1690	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Yesterday, colleagues around the table made impressive presentations, setting out some of the downside risks of the decision we will be making in a few hours.	23	2
201512	1691	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	I thought as I listened that it was a privilege to be a member of this Committee as we discuss the nation’s monetary policy with a seriousness and a level that is appropriate to the significance of our task.	23	2
201512	1692	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	For that we owe and express thanks not only to one another, but also and particularly to the Chair and to the staff.	23	2
201512	1693	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	We said in March that we would move to raise interest rates as long as labor market conditions continued to improve and when members of the Committee were reasonably confident that inflation would return to its 2 percent target level over the medium term.	23	2
201512	1694	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	I believe those conditions have been met.	23	2
201512	1695	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	This conclusion depends on my belief that, over the medium term, the Phillips-curve relationship will reassert itself, and I think we are beginning to see some signs of that in the behavior of labor compensation, but only faintly so.	23	2
201512	1696	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	What other factors are relevant?	23	2
201512	1697	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Let me list only eight.	23	2
201512	1698	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	One, the increase in the interest rate is very small.	23	2
201512	1699	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	We will be moving from an ultraexpansionary monetary policy to an extremely expansionary monetary policy.	23	2
201512	1700	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Two, what happens next?	23	2
201512	1701	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	On that issue, members of the FOMC have been clear, as I just said, that we expect a gradual process of normalization and recognize the possibility that the rate may also decline.	23	2
201512	1702	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Three, we should not minimize the uncertainties we always face about the future, especially in a situation such as the one we face today when we’re about to implement a new monetary policy mechanism designed to operate with our extremely large portfolio and with large countries, including China and Brazil, facing major economic policy challenges.	23	2
201512	1703	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Four, the Federal Reserve System has developed and tested the approach we will be using to raise the interest rate.	23	2
201512	1704	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	At one stage, it seemed useful to describe it as a corridor system, but it is more accurate to describe it as a two-story system.	23	2
201512	1705	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Not only has the system been tested, but the staff has also developed other mechanisms for use in a circumstance under which the two- story system does not do the job it is designed and expected to do.	23	2
201512	1706	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Five, we’re sending a signal not only about our expectations regarding the future, but also about what has been achieved so far:  a return to near normal in the labor market, which is an extraordinary success for the policies this Committee has implemented since the end of 2008— but, six, at a time when largely temporary forces are keeping the inflation rate significantly below its target level.	23	2
201512	1707	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	There are good reasons to expect that the continuing declines in the price of energy and in the appreciation of the dollar are temporary.	23	2
201512	1708	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Seven, many colleagues are concerned about indications that the expected rate of inflation has declined somewhat during recent months.	23	2
201512	1709	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	I am also concerned, but I think that the more significant phenomenon is how little expected inflation has declined over the very long period that the actual inflation rate has been well below the target level of 2 percent.	23	2
201512	1710	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Eight, the economy has, during the course of the past year, withstood powerful headwinds and continued to increase employment, with a core PCE inflation rate that has remained above 1 percent and expected inflation rates that have stayed close to 2 percent.	23	2
201512	1711	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	In sum, our economy has done a superb, albeit not perfect, job in the continuing task of restoring a more normal labor market.	23	2
201512	1712	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	And I believe we will, over the medium term, return to the vicinity of our target inflation rate and to a situation in which the interest rate will again play its role in the allocation of resources, including the allocation between financial activities and real investment.	23	2
201512	1713	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Why move now?	23	2
201512	1714	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Why not wait longer?	23	2
201512	1715	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	First, as the Chair has emphasized, our actions become effective with a lag.	23	2
201512	1716	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Second, there are some signs of accumulating financial stability problems.	23	2
201512	1717	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	And, third, the signal we will be sending will reinforce the fact that our economic situation is continuing to normalize.	23	2
201512	1718	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	It is, of course, our duty to consider the many ways our expectations could be driven off track, but we also have to assign probabilities to the shocks that might drive us off track and to our ability to deal with them.	23	2
201512	1719	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	My conclusion is that we’re more likely to continue along a positive track and to withstand the negative forces with which we will certainly have to contend as events unfold and which may temporarily drive us off course.	23	2
201512	1720	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	I’d like next to turn, but briefly, to a few issues that continue to crop up.	23	2
201512	1721	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	First, are we about to repeat the experience of 1936 and 1937, as one hears?	23	2
201512	1722	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	No.	23	2
201512	1723	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	The financial system is currently in good shape and will remain in good shape so long as we successfully manage financial stability, as I believe we’re doing now.	23	2
201512	1724	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	And, no, because there is no intention of tightening fiscal policy, as was done 80 years ago.	23	2
201512	1725	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Second, are we too late to move?	23	2
201512	1726	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	No.	23	2
201512	1727	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	The financial system is basically in good shape, although there are some signs of instability in very localized instances, and employment continues to grow.	23	2
201512	1728	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	But what if growth ceases?	23	2
201512	1729	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Then we can reduce the interest rate.	23	2
201512	1730	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	I do not expect that we will have to do that, but I do believe we need to reconsider the argument that we should stay at the zero lower bound because if we try to get away from it, we will have to return to it.	23	2
201512	1731	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	That will always be a possibility for any country that decides to raise the interest rate above the ZLB, for negative shocks happen.	23	2
201512	1732	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	But that possibility should not keep us at the zero lower bound forever.	23	2
201512	1733	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	It is not enough to give an example of countries that have had to return to the zero lower bound.	23	2
201512	1734	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	One has to consider the expected value of trying to move away versus the expected value of staying put.	23	2
201512	1735	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	The possibility that we will have to move back should not keep us at the zero lower bound forever, for the outlook is positive, and positive shocks also happen even if, by definition, we do not know when shocks will happen.	23	2
201512	1736	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Third, isn’t the rest of the world in too fragile a state for us to move?	23	2
201512	1737	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Most of the rest of the world is not doing well, but this economy has succeeded in increasing employment at a rapid rate despite the appreciation of the dollar and the decline in net exports.	23	2
201512	1738	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Expectations are that the growth rate of foreign countries will increase in 2016.	23	2
201512	1739	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Further, the exchange rate will cease appreciating at some point—and we saw some suggestions yesterday that it could be soon.	23	2
201512	1740	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	I believe that as we look to the future, we should address several worrisome developments with respect to our ability to do our job, particularly the constraints placed on our ability to act as the lender of last resort in a crisis and the shortage of policy tools to deal with financial stability.	23	2
201512	1741	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	There are other monetary policy topics we will need to address in the period ahead, particularly the role of forward guidance, the monetary mechanism toward which we are evolving, and the possibilities of finding new tools to deal with the zero lower bound.	23	2
201512	1742	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	So, to conclude, we’re setting out on a new journey with the same goals we’ve always had—maximum employment, stable prices, and financial stability.	23	2
201512	1743	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	The journey is difficult and daunting, but we can take some comfort from the successes of Federal Reserve policy since the end of 2008, even while we need to remember the warning sent by the fact that there was a global financial crisis that began in September 2008.	23	2
201512	1744	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	As always, we’re operating in a world in flux.	23	2
201512	1745	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	At this time, a world that, after the historical entry of China into the modern world economy and the likely entry down the road of India into the modern world economy, the world may well be more like the world economy of the pre-BRICS era than we expected just a few years ago.	23	2
201512	1746	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Of course, we are not the only policymakers whose actions affect the economy.	23	2
201512	1747	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Of course, we do not have some of the tools that we need to manage financial stability.	23	2
201512	1748	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	But we have a job to do—monetary policy—and we have the tools to manage it.	23	2
201512	1749	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	I expect that we will continue to do our job well, and that the decision we are likely to take today will be part of doing that job well.	23	2
201512	1750	2015-12-16	meeting	FISCHER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201512	1751	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	23	2
201512	1752	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	President Lockhart.	23	2
201512	1753	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201512	1754	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	I support alternative B, and I’m satisfied that the statement as written will serve as effective communication of the Committee’s momentous decision in alternative B.	23	2
201512	1755	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	I’d like to spend a couple of minutes sharing some anticipatory thoughts on possible implications of the sentence in paragraph 4 that begins “In light of the current shortfall of inflation.”	23	2
201512	1756	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	This sentence calls out inflation as the focus of attention as we go through 2016 and, since the Committee’s decisions will be data dependent, suggests that the inflation data will significantly influence subsequent policy rate decisions.	23	2
201512	1757	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	The SEP dot chart looks as though it will set up an expectation of rate increases on a schedule of every other meeting.	23	2
201512	1758	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	The word “gradual,” used twice in the alternative B statement, will, to some extent, take its definition from the SEP.	23	2
201512	1759	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	So, assuming a move in January is a virtual nonstarter, which I do, the expectation will be for a second policy rate move in March.	23	2
201512	1760	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	In the spirit of an “eyes wide open” approach, I think it’s worth considering what we will likely know at the time of the March meeting.	23	2
201512	1761	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	We will have the February CPI data arriving on the second day of that meeting.	23	2
201512	1762	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	We will have PCE price data only through January.	23	2
201512	1763	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	With the continuing softness in oil, gasoline, and commodity prices, it seems to me likely that the inflation data we will have in hand will be very weak.	23	2
201512	1764	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	The Tealbook, in fact, suggests zero for the headline inflation number for the first quarter.	23	2
201512	1765	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	At this juncture, I have no reason to dispute the Tealbook projection.	23	2
201512	1766	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	The Chair pointed out yesterday that we might have a small uptick in the year-over-year headline and core PCE readings because January 2015 was extremely weak.	23	2
201512	1767	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	Even so, an inflation-data-dependent decision to raise the policy rate a second time in March could be problematic, it seems to me.	23	2
201512	1768	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	As I said at the beginning of my comments, I support the statement as written.	23	2
201512	1769	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	Nonetheless, I’m a little concerned about how we will operationalize the criterion of actual and expected progress toward our inflation goal in the early part of next year.	23	2
201512	1770	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	I doubt we will have inflation statistics that are supportive of a conclusion that progress is being made.	23	2
201512	1771	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	We may have to rely once more on employment data, along with the faith-based expectations drawn from our forecasts.	23	2
201512	1772	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	The emphasis may have to remain on the expected, rather than the actual, inflation evidence.	23	2
201512	1773	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	My overall point is a small one, really:  It’s one thing to project from the SEP exercise a forecast-based median level of the funds rate at year-end 2016.	23	2
201512	1774	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	It may well be another thing to make post-liftoff rate decisions in real time, especially in March, before those forecasts have had much validation.	23	2
201512	1775	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	So before the ink is long dry on today’s statement, we may well be advised to start thinking about how to make subsequent policy decisions and, very importantly, how to communicate the nuances of data dependence when the data are less complete or more ambiguous than we would like.	23	2
201512	1776	2015-12-16	meeting	LOCKHART	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201512	1777	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	23	2
201512	1778	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	President Lacker.	23	2
201512	1779	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201512	1780	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	For the past several meetings, I’ve been convinced that economic conditions warranted an increase in our target federal funds rate range.	23	2
201512	1781	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	This was based on a sense that labor markets were in line with our best assessments of what constitutes full employment and on confidence that inflation will move back to 2 percent once the most recent disinflationary impulse has passed.	23	2
201512	1782	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	Since then, as I discussed in our earlier go- round, the economic reports for the United States haven’t appreciably altered that assessment.	23	2
201512	1783	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	So I continue to see a rate increase as well justified, and I support alternative B.	23	2
201512	1784	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	It’s great to be able to say that.	23	2
201512	1785	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	With this first rate increase effectively behind us, market attention is going to focus on the guidance we provide in the statement regarding the prospective funds rate path.	23	2
201512	1786	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	Many Committee participants, myself included, have been saying that they expect the pace of the funds rate increases to be gradual.	23	2
201512	1787	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	As a result, market participants probably expect to see the word “gradual” in the statement.	23	2
201512	1788	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	As drafted, the statement does a great job of that.	23	2
201512	1789	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	It includes it twice—once in paragraph 2, in which we refer to “gradual adjustments in the stance of monetary policy,” and then again down in paragraph 4, in which we refer to “only gradual increases in the federal funds rate.”	23	2
201512	1790	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	These are both new elements.	23	2
201512	1791	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	My sense is that this statement could well push down the expected path of short-term rates.	23	2
201512	1792	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	I don’t think pushing down the expected path of short-term rates would be a desirable outcome.	23	2
201512	1793	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	As we saw yesterday, markets already expect a funds rate path substantially below the path embodied in the median SEP or the staff’s forecast.	23	2
201512	1794	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	And according to the Tealbook, the market’s uncertainty about the pace of tightening is well below the levels seen during the previous tightening episodes, and I thought that evidence was quite striking.	23	2
201512	1795	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	Under those circumstances, we should avoid pushing down market expectations of the funds rate path even further, but I’m willing to support the statement as written.	23	2
201512	1796	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	However, I think we’re running a risk here of exacerbating the disconnect between the market’s expectations of the funds rate path and ours, and I hope that doesn’t happen.	23	2
201512	1797	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	I also see a risk that emphasizing a gradual path could reinforce the excessive sense of certainty in markets about that path, and that that could impede the adjustment of market expectations if the economic outlook starts to change materially in either direction, as Governor Fischer emphasized.	23	2
201512	1798	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	We should provide guidance to markets about how we will react to incoming data whenever we can, and I think the new sentence in paragraph 4 that President Lockhart discussed, which refers to the current shortfall of inflation from 2 percent, seems to be a constructive element that does so.	23	2
201512	1799	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	But a heavy stress on the word “gradual” could dampen the market’s responsiveness to incoming data.	23	2
201512	1800	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	If anything, based on the Tealbook’s assessment of the market’s current lack of uncertainty about rates, I think it would be worthwhile to encourage markets to be less certain about the future path of rates.	23	2
201512	1801	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	I have a suggestion regarding communications for use either in the press conference or more generally for all of us, and this is a “bipartisan” suggestion.	23	2
201512	1802	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	Lately, the answer to questions about the pace of increases seems to be a one-word mantra, “gradual.”	23	2
201512	1803	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	And it seems to have emerged as this cycle’s replacement for the two-word mantra of “measured pace,” which, during the past tightening cycle, came to be understood to mean precisely a quarter-point increase per meeting.	23	2
201512	1804	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	So I’d suggest that our mantra should be a four-word phrase, “gradual but data dependent,” in order to emphasize that responding to economic conditions takes precedent over implied past promises to proceed at any particular pace.	23	2
201512	1805	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	In other words, we shouldn’t say the word “gradual” without saying “but data dependent.”	23	2
201512	1806	2015-12-16	meeting	LACKER	Thank you.	23	2
201512	1807	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	23	2
201512	1808	2015-12-16	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Tarullo.	23	2
201512	1809	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201512	1810	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	As everyone will have inferred from my remarks yesterday, I don’t think it’s appropriate policy to raise rates today.	23	2
201512	1811	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	Even if one is inclined toward the transitory factors hypothesis, today seems an odd moment to declare reasonable confidence that inflation will return to the Committee’s stated 2 percent target, what with the further declines in oil prices, the expected extension of strong dollar effects, the CPI reading earlier in the week, and the number of concerns expressed here yesterday about inflation expectations.	23	2
201512	1812	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	In light of the number of important questions about whether inflation dynamics have changed in recent years, as well as about the labor market, I continue to believe it more prudent for the Committee to act more on evidence than on faith that traditional economic patterns and relationships will reassert themselves.	23	2
201512	1813	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	Again, I don’t deny that these patterns may reemerge, but it’s far from certain.	23	2
201512	1814	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	And with numerous tightening tools available in an economy that is not running very hot but with an unappealing set of options were more accommodation to be needed, I think it wise to be particularly certain of the directions of inflation and the economy before raising rates, thereby diminishing the chances of this latter eventuality.	23	2
201512	1815	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	My policy preference is captured fairly well by alternative A, though I would remove the sentence in paragraph 3 about providing additional accommodation.	23	2
201512	1816	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	Of course, I’ve asked myself what the best argument for acting today is and have listened to or read the views of many others on this topic.	23	2
201512	1817	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	It seems the best reason to act lies not in the economics we face at today’s meeting, but in the fact that many on the Committee and, more recently, a particularly influential member thereof have intimated that we’re going to do so.	23	2
201512	1818	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	I’ve noted in the past that one shouldn’t follow through on an ill-advised policy just because one has said one might adopt that policy, but I have to admit that, at this point, the credibility of the FOMC is at some risk since many in the markets and the public believe that the FOMC promised September, then didn’t act, and has now promised December.	23	2
201512	1819	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	This poses some disturbing institutional issues—most important, the question of whether the Committee is to be pushed into action through arguably premature or overbroad public statements.	23	2
201512	1820	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	That is an important issue, and maybe it should bear discussion at some point in the Committee.	23	2
201512	1821	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	But, speaking for myself at this meeting, I wasn’t a part of this, and, as many will recall, I’ve advised against this pattern of frequent public comments with frequent references to particular meetings.	23	2
201512	1822	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	Despite all of that, I will reluctantly go along with alternative B today for two reasons.	23	2
201512	1823	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	First, there is the institutional reality that there’s enormous significance attached out there to a member of the Board voting against the Chair’s position.	23	2
201512	1824	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	Perhaps this shouldn’t be this way and we might be better off with the culture of the Bank of England’s Monetary Policy Committee, but reality is what it is.	23	2
201512	1825	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	This moment of liftoff after seven years would be a particularly bad time to enter a dissent and thereby risk the Chair’s leadership position at a critical moment in monetary policy, which may face some considerable challenges in the months ahead.	23	2
201512	1826	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	Second, the Committee’s decision today as shaped by the Chair is, at least by its terms, not just for the rate rise, but also for an approach to monetary policy over the next year, one that is presumptively gradual and, with the addition of the language on inflation to paragraph 4, emphasizes what I’ve been suggesting—that is, it pays particular attention to whether inflation plays out as today’s SEP suggests it will.	23	2
201512	1827	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	I requested such language and feel that its inclusion provides some basis for my going along with what is a broader policy orientation than just the federal funds rate increase.	23	2
201512	1828	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	And, as I suggested yesterday, the transitory factors hypothesis is plausible.	23	2
201512	1829	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	I hope this orientation will mean that I’ll be closer to the majority of the Committee in assessing the economy—and inflation, in particular—as we go forward.	23	2
201512	1830	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	After all, even though I do think some secular changes in the economy may be playing an important role in affecting inflation, my baseline expectation is still for a gradual upward movement next year.	23	2
201512	1831	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	Because of the questions that I discussed yesterday, I just don’t have enough confidence to act on those expectations right now.	23	2
201512	1832	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	I was going to omit this statement.	23	2
201512	1833	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	I had written this out last night, and I crossed it out this morning.	23	2
201512	1834	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	But, having just listened to several other comments, I recognize that others may differ, and I may be left concluding at a future meeting that faith has trumped empirics too much.	23	2
201512	1835	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	I have to confess, I already hear some effort to undermine the language that has been inserted, so I’m afraid I do anticipate that I may have some differences with the majority of the Committee in the future.	23	2

201512	1838	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	My focus on evidence and pragmatics is not one way.	23	2

201512	1840	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	If, for example, inflation were to begin moving well ahead of what the Committee expects in a way that suggested a trend, I would not be averse to taking quicker action despite my current instinct that things have changed in the economy in some pretty basic ways over the past 10 or so years.	23	2
201512	1841	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	And it’s for that reason that I actually would not want any stronger language in the statement committing us to a gradual approach or to reinvestment.	23	2

201512	1843	2015-12-16	meeting	TARULLO	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
